Hajj Bequest: Hometown vs. Place of Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj bequest starting point

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the starting point for Hajj from a bequest when the testator dies en route, and explain the legal reasoning (dalil) behind each position.

Core Idea
The starting point for a bequeathed Hajj depends on whether the journey was an act of worship or merely travel.

When a person bequeaths Hajj but dies on the way, a key question arises: should the proxy start from the hometown or from the place of death? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions. Their reasoning turns on the legal nature of the journey—whether it counts as an act of worship (qurba) or not. By studying this case, you will learn how the Hanafi school uses qiyas and intention to resolve practical issues in wills.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the legal problem: a testator bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him, but he dies en route. From which location should the proxy begin the Hajj?
This is a sub-issue of kitab al-wasaya.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds: from the hometown if funds suffice, otherwise from where funds suffice. The two companions (Sahibayn) hold: from the place of death, regardless of sufficiency.
The difference affects cost and route.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's qiyas
Abu Hanifa analogizes to a merchant who dies on a trade journey: since the journey was not for worship, the Hajj must start from home. Similarly, the testator's journey was 'other than Hajj' because he died before completing it.
The journey's purpose is key: mere travel vs. worship.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn argue that the journey was intended as Hajj, so it counts as an act of worship (qurba). The obligation of covering the distance is proportionally fulfilled; thus the starting point is where death occurred, as if he were from that place.
Intention transforms the legal nature of the journey.
5
Note the practical difference
If funds are limited, Abu Hanifa requires starting from home if possible; the Sahibayn allow starting from the death location. Later Hanafi practice generally favors the Sahibayn view.
This is an example of thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند أبي حنيفة " إن بلغ نفقته ذلك ، وإلا فمن حيث تبلغ، وعندهما يحج من حيث مات، وإن لم تبلغ النفقة ذلك، فمن حيث تبلغ. قوله : عند أبي حنيفة له ؛ له : إنَّ الوصية تنصرف إلى الحج من بلده ؛ لأنه لما مات قبل إتمام العمل صار خروجه بغير الحج كما إذا خرج تاجراً فمات في بعض الطريق يحج من منزله، فكذلك هاهنا. ولهما : إنَّ السفر نية الحج ، وقع قربةً وسقط فرضُ قطع المسافة بقدر سفره، وقد وقع أجره على الله، فيبتدئ من مكان مات فيه كأنه من أهله، بخلاف سفر التجارة ؛ لأنه لم يقع قربة، فيحج عنه من بلده ، كذا في بعض حواشي «الهداية».
According to Abu Hanifa: ‘If his (the deceased's) expense reaches that, then from there; otherwise from where it reaches. And according to them (the two companions): He performs Hajj from where he died, even if the expense does not reach that; so from where it reaches.’ [Commentary] His statement: According to Abu Hanifa: … Indeed, the will is directed to Hajj from his hometown; because when he died before completing the action, his departure became other than Hajj, just as if he went out as a merchant and died on the way, he is performed Hajj from his home, so here too. And according to them: Indeed, the journey is the intention of Hajj; it occurred as an act of worship and the obligation of covering the distance fell according to his travel, and his reward is with Allah, so he begins from the place where he died as if he were from his family, unlike a trading journey because it did not occur as worship, so Hajj is performed for him from his hometown. As in some glosses of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the execution of a bequest for Hajj when the testator dies en route. The ruling is part of the chapter on wills (kitab al-wasaya). The text first states the positions: Abu Hanifa holds that the Hajj pilgrimage should be performed from the testator's hometown if the funds suffice; otherwise from where the funds allow. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it should be performed from the place of death, regardless of sufficiency of funds. The commentary explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa analogizes the deceased to a merchant who dies on a trade journey – since his departure was not purely for worship, the Hajj must begin from home. The two companions, however, consider the journey itself an act of worship (qurba) due to the intention of Hajj, so the obligation of traveling a certain distance is already fulfilled to the extent traveled; thus the Hajj starts where death occurred. This highlights a difference in how they view the nature of the journey and the effect of intention. The passage is a gloss on al-Hidayah, showing the ongoing scholarly refinement.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will directing how a portion of the deceased's estate is to be used after death.
الحج (al-hajj): The pilgrimage to Mecca, a fard obligation for those who can afford it physically and financially.
قربة (qurba): An act of worship that brings one closer to Allah; here it is used to describe a journey with the intention of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From the place where he died
C) From where the funds allow

Key Takeaway
The starting point for a bequeathed Hajj depends on whether the journey is considered an act of worship (Sahibayn) or mere travel (Abu Hanifa), with the later Hanafi practice favoring the Sahibayn view.

Division of One-Third Among Two Legatees: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Rulings on dividing one-third bequest among two legatees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on dividing a bequest of one-third between two legatees and apply the method of mutual claim to resolve competing bequests.

Core Idea
When two legatees claim the same one-third, Abu Hanifa halves it; Sahibayn quarter it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about apportioning a one-third bequest when two beneficiaries are named for overlapping amounts. The commentary examines three scenarios and then focuses on the third case where one legatee is given one-third and the other is given 'the whole third.' The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, reveals deep principles of conflict resolution in bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage begins with three cases of multiple legatees. For the first two, the division is agreed upon. Note the third scenario where the dispute arises.
The third scenario: one legatee gets one-third, the other gets 'the entire third' (i.e., each is bequeathed the same one-third).
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Abu Hanifa says the one-third is halved (half for each legatee). Understand his reasoning: when two conflicting bequests cover the same asset, they are treated equally.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the third is quartered: one-quarter to the first, three-quarters to the second. Understand their reasoning: the second legatee has a stronger claim because he is given the entire third.
4
Examine the mutual claim analysis
The commentary delves into the method of mutual claim (munaza'a) to resolve the dispute. Abu Yusuf attempted a sixths division, but Al-Hasan al-Saghir corrected it to a quarters division. Trace the arithmetic: the one-third is 4/12 of the whole, divided into halves (2/12 each), then the remaining 8/12 are claimed by the second legatee, but the first also claims a share, leading to 3/12 for the first and 9/12 for the second.
This method respects that the heirs' consent does not enlarge the one-third.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi authorities, as cited in al-Haqa'iq, al-Qahistani, and Radd al-Muhtar, endorse the quartering view of Sahibayn. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Thus, the student should learn the quartering method as the relied-upon rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوصية بالثلث (في) وصيته بثلث ماله لزيد ومثلِهِ لآخر، ولم يجيزوا ، بنصف ثلث بينهما ، وبثلث له وسدس لآخر، بثلث ، وبثلثه لبكر وكله لآخر ينصف ، وقالا : يربع) ، قال أبو حنيفة : الوصية بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم يجز الورثة " قد وقع باطلا ، [1] قوله : في وصيته بثلث ماله.... الخ ؛ صورته : إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد، ومثله لآخر، ولم تجز الورثة، فثلثه بينهما نصفين اتفاقاً ، وإن أوصى بثلث لزيد وبسدس ماله لآخر، فالثلث بينهما أثلاثاً اتفاقاً أيضاً. أما في صورة إجازة الورثة فظاهر، وإن أوصى بثلث ماله لبكر، وكله لآخر، فينصف : أي ثلثه بينهما نصفان عند أ أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : يربع : أي فالثلث بينهما ربعه لبكر وثلاثة أرباعه لآخر. (٢) قوله : إذا لم يجز الورثة ؛ فإن أجازوا فعندهما يقسم الكل أرباعاً، ولا نص فيه عنه، ، فقال أبو يوسف : قياس قوله أن يسدَّس بطريق المنازعة ؛ لأنَّ الثلثين لصاحب الكلّ، فكان نزاعُهُما في الثلث، فنصفُ النصف الذي . هو السدس لصاحب الثلث، والباقي للآخر. وقال الحسن : إن هذا تخريج قبيح ؛ لاستوائهم [مع سهم] صاحب الثلث في حال الإجازة وعدمها، وهو السدس. فالصحيح أن يربع بطريق المنازعة بأن يقسم الثلث أوّلاً ، وهو أربعة من اثنى عشر بينهما نصفين ؛ لأنَّ إجازتهم غير مؤثرة في قدر الثلث، وبقي الثلثان ثمانية أسهم يدعيها صاحب الكل، وسهمين منها صاحب الثلث، ليتم الثلث، فَتُسَلِّمُ الستة لصاحب الكل، ويتنازعان في السهمين بنصفين، فيحصل ثلاثة أسهم لصاحب الثلث ، والباقي للآخر. كما في «الحقائق»، وغيره، «قهستاني». قلت : وعلى قولهما يلزم استواء حالتي الاجازة وعدمها. هكذا في ردا د المحتار). (۱) رد المحتار» (٦ : ٦٦٧).
Chapter of Will of One-Third: (In) his will of one-third of his wealth to Zaid and the like of it to another, and they (heirs) did not consent, then half of the one-third between them. And (if) one-third to him and one-sixth to another, then (the third apportioned as) one-third. And (if) his one-third to Bakr and all of it (the third) to another, then it is halved (i.e., half each according to Abu Hanifa). The two (companions) said: it is quartered. Abu Hanifa said: The bequest of more than one-third, if the heirs do not consent, is void. [Commentary] His statement: 'In his will...' etc.; its form: If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zaid and the like to another, and the heirs do not consent, then his one-third is between them in halves by agreement. And if he bequeaths one-third to Zaid and one-sixth of his wealth to another, then the one-third is between them in thirds by agreement also. As for the case of the heirs’ consent, it is clear. But if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Bakr and the entire (third) to another, then he halves (i.e., the third is halved according to Abu Hanifa). The two said: He quarters, i.e., the one-third between them is a quarter for Bakr and three-quarters for the other. (2) His statement: When the heirs do not consent; then if they consent, according to the two the whole is divided into fourths, and there is no text from him (Abu Hanifa) on it. So Abu Yusuf said: The analogical consequence of his statement is that it is divided into sixths via mutual claim (muzara'a): because two-thirds belong to the owner of the whole (the one who bequeathed the entire third?), so their dispute is over the one-third, so half of the half which is one-sixth goes to the owner of the one-third, and the rest to the other. Al-Hasan said: This is a bad derivation, because they are equal with the share of the owner of the one-third in the case of consent and non-consent, and it is one-sixth. The correct is that it is quartered via mutual claim: the one-third is divided first, which is four out of twelve, between them in halves because the consent does not affect the extent of the one-third; and the remaining two-thirds are eight shares which the owner of the whole claims, and two shares of them are claimed by the owner of the one-third to complete the third. So six are given to the owner of the whole, and they dispute over the two shares in halves, resulting in three shares for the owner of the one-third and the rest for the other. As in al-Haqa'iq and others, al-Qahistani. I say: According to their statement, the two states of consent and non-consent become equal. Thus in Radd al-Muhtar (6:667).
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage discusses the division of the one-third bequest when multiple legatees are named and the heirs do not consent (or do consent). It begins with three scenarios: (1) one-third to Zaid and one-third to another: the third is split equally by agreement. (2) one-third to Zaid and one-sixth to another: the third is split in proportion 2:1 (two-thirds of the third to Zaid, one-third to the other) by agreement. (3) one-third to Bakr and the entire third to another (i.e., one person is given the full one-third, and another is also given the same one-third): here a dispute arises. Imam Abu Hanifa says to halve the third (half each), while the two companions (Sahibayn) say to quarter it (one-quarter for the first, three-quarters for the second). The commentary then addresses what happens if the heirs consent (ijaza). The two companions divide the entire estate into fourths? Actually the text says 'if they consent, according to the two the whole is divided into fourths' – but the phrase is confusing. It then mentions Abu Yusuf's opinion that by qiyas, the division should be sixths based on mutual claim. Al-Hasan al-Saghir criticizes this as a bad derivation. The correct method, per the later scholars, is to divide the one-third first (which is 4/12 of the whole) into halves between the two legatees (since the consent does not enlarge the one-third), then the remaining two-thirds (8/12) are claimed by the 'owner of the whole' (the second legatee), but the first legatee also claims a share of that to reach his full third? The detailed calculation yields three shares out of twelve for the first legatee and nine for the second. This intricate reasoning shows the high level of dispute resolution in Hanafi fiqh, using the concept of mutual claims (muzara'a). The passage concludes that according to the two companions' view, the result is the same whether the heirs consent or not.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum a testator can bequeath without heirs' consent.
الإجازة (al-ijaza): Consent or permission by the heirs to allow a bequest exceeding one-third or to validate a disputed division.
المنازعة (al-munaza'a): Mutual claim or contention, a legal procedure used to resolve competing claims on the same asset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The first gets one-third of the one-third and the second gets two-thirds

D) The first gets one-sixth and the second gets the rest

Key Takeaway
When two legatees are named for the same one-third, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that the third is divided into four parts: one for the first and three for the second.

Dividing the Third Among Multiple Legatees: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing the third when bequests exceed the third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on dividing the third when a bequest exceeds one-third and heirs do not consent, and apply the calculation in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa voids the excess entirely; the Sahibayn proportionally reduce it – leading to different shares from the third.

When a testator bequeaths more than one-third of his estate and the heirs do not consent, the bequest exceeding the third is void. But how should the remaining third be divided among multiple legatees? The Hanafi masters disagree. This lesson explains the dispute and its arithmetic application, using the technical term 'darb' (striking) to calculate shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the bequests: two legatees, one bequest of 1/3, another of 1/3, 1/6, or 'the whole'. Note when the heirs do not consent.
The dispute arises only when the total bequest exceeds one-third, e.g., 1/3 + whole = 4/3 > 1/3.
2
Recall the agreed cases
When both bequests are within the third (e.g., two 1/3s, or 1/3 and 1/6), the schools agree on simple proportional division: halves for two 1/3s; thirds (2:1) for 1/3 and 1/6.
No dispute when sum ≤ 1/3.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that any bequest exceeding the third is entirely void. Thus the legatee of 'the whole' is treated as if bequeathed only one-third, so both share the actual third equally.
Result: each gets 1/6 of total estate.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that only the excess over the third is void. The legatee of the whole still has a claim in the third proportional to his full bequest. Thus the third is divided into four parts: one part to the third-legator, three parts to the whole-legator.
Result: third-legator gets 1/12, whole-legator gets 1/4 of total.
5
Understand 'darb' (striking)
The technical term 'darb' refers to multiplying the legatee's proportional share in the bequest by the available third. Under Abu Hanifa, each legatee has 1/2 share, so each 'strikes' 1/2 in the third, getting 1/6 of the total. Under the Sahibayn, the whole-legator has 3/4 share, so strikes 3/4 in third, getting 3/16? Wait, careful: the third is 1/3 of total. 3/4 of 1/3 = 1/4 of total. Yes.
This arithmetic is essential for accurate distribution.

Source Text

أما في صورة إجازة الورثة فظاهر، وإن أوصى بثلث ماله لبكر، وكله لآخر، فينصف : أي ثلثه بينهما نصفان عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : يربع : أي فالثلث بينهما ربعه لبكر وثلاثة أرباعه لآخر.
فإن أجازوا فعندهما يقسم الكل أرباعاً، ولا نص فيه عنه، فقال أبو يوسف : قياس قوله أن يسدَّس بطريق المنازعة ؛ لأنَّ الثلثين لصاحب الكلّ، فكان نزاعُهُما في الثلث، فنصفُ النصف الذي . هو السدس لصاحب الثلث، والباقي للآخر.
وقال الحسن : إن هذا تخريج قبيح ؛ لاستوائهم [مع سهم] صاحب الثلث في حال الإجازة وعدمها، وهو السدس. فالصحيح أن يربع بطريق المنازعة بأن يقسم الثلث أوّلاً ، وهو أربعة من اثنى عشر بينهما نصفين ؛ لأنَّ إجازتهم غير مؤثرة في قدر الثلث، وبقي الثلثان ثمانية أسهم يدعيها صاحب الكل، وسهمين منها صاحب الثلث، ليتم الثلث، فَتُسَلِّمُ الستة لصاحب الكل، ويتنازعان في السهمين بنصفين، فيحصل ثلاثة أسهم لصاحب الثلث ، والباقي للآخر. كما في «الحقائق»، وغيره، «قهستاني». قلت : وعلى قولهما يلزم استواء حالتي الاجازة وعدمها. هكذا في ردا د المحتار).
ولا يُضْرَبُ الموصى له بأكثر الثلث من عند أبي حنيفة له فكأنه أوصى بالثلث لكلِّ واحد ، فينصفُ الثُّلث بينهما، وقالا : إنما يبطل الزائد على الثلث، بمعنى أن الموصى له لا يستحقه حقاً للورثة ، لكن يعتبر في أنَّ الموصى له يأخذ من الثلث بحصة ذلك الزائد، إذ لا موجب لإبطال هذا المعني، فخرج الثلث ثلاثة، فالثلث واحد، والكل ثلاثة صارت أربعة ، فيقسم الثلث بهذه السهام، فهذا مبني على أصل مختلف بينهم، وهو قوله : ولا يُضْرَب الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث عند أبي حنيفة ) ، المراد بالضَّرْبِ الضرب المصطلح بين الحساب، فإنَّه إذا أَوْصَى بالثلث والكلِّ، فعند أبي حنيفة له سهام الوصية اثنان، لكلِّ واحدٍ ،نصف ، يَضْرِبُ النَّصف في ثُلُثِ المال ، فالنصف في الثلث يكون نصف الثلث، وهو السدس ، فلكل سدس المال
فمعنى «المتن» لا يأخذ الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث بما زاد على الثلث ؛ لأن قوله : بأكثرَ ؛ إن تعلّق بالموصى له كان مفعول لا يضرب محذوفاً، وهو مما زاد على الثلث، وإن تعلق بلا يضرب كان صلة الموصى له محذوفاً، كما زاد ونحوه. فالحاصل أن للموصى له بما زاد من الثلث إذا لم يجز الورثة الوصية لا يأخذ من الثلث بقدر نصيبه من الكلِّ على تقدير الإجازة، بل يكون هو والموصى له بالثلث سواء عند الأعظم. كذا في «الكوسجيّة».
Chapter of bequest of one-third. In his bequest of one-third of his wealth to Zayd and the like to another, and they did not consent, half of the third between them. And in one-third to him and one-sixth to another, one-third. And in one-third to Bakr and all of it to another, halves. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: fourths. Abu Hanifa said: A bequest of more than a third when the heirs do not consent is void. Its picture: if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zayd and the like to another, and the heirs do not consent, then his third is between them in halves by agreement. And if he bequeaths one-third to Zayd and one-sixth of his wealth to another, then the third between them in thirds by agreement also. As for the case of consent of the heirs, it is apparent. And if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Bakr and all of it to another, then halves: i.e., his third between them in halves according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: fourths: i.e., the third between them is a quarter to Bakr and three-quarters to another. If they consent, then according to them (the two companions) the whole is divided into fourths, and there is no text from him (Abu Hanifa) about it. Abu Yusuf said: the analogy of his statement is that it is divided into sixths by way of mutual claim because two-thirds belong to the claimant of all, so their dispute is over the third, so half of the half which is one-sixth is for the claimant of one-third, and the rest for the other. Al-Hasan said: This is an ugly derivation because they are equal with the share of the claimant of the third in the case of consent and its absence, and it is one-sixth. The correct is to divide into fourths by way of mutual claim by dividing the third first, which is four out of twelve, between them in halves; because their consent does not affect the amount of the third, and the remaining two-thirds are eight shares claimed by the claimant of all, and two shares of them by the claimant of the third to complete the third. So six are given to the claimant of all, and they dispute over the two shares in halves, resulting in three shares for the claimant of the third and the rest for the other. As in al-Haqa'iq and others, Qahastani. I say: according to their statement, the two cases of consent and its absence become equal. This is in Radd al-Muhtar. And the legatee is not struck (yudrab) with more than the third according to Abu Hanifa, for him it is as if he bequeathed the third to each one, so the third is divided in halves between them. And they (the two companions) said: only the excess over the third is void, meaning the legatee does not deserve it as a right of the heirs, but it is considered that the legatee takes from the third in proportion to that excess, since there is no cause to nullify this meaning. So the third is three, the third is one, and the whole is three, making four, so the third is divided according to these shares. This is based on a fundamental difference among them, which is his statement: 'The legatee is not struck with more than the third according to Abu Hanifa'. The intended meaning of 'struck' is the technical term in arithmetic. For if he bequeaths the third and the whole, according to Abu Hanifa, the legatee has two shares of the bequest, half for each, so he strikes half in the third of the wealth, thus half in the third becomes half of the third, which is one-sixth, so each gets one-sixth of the wealth. So the meaning of the matn is: the legatee does not take more than the third for what exceeds the third; because his saying 'with more' if it is attached to the legatee, the object of 'does not strike' is omitted, i.e., what exceeds the third, and if it is attached to 'does not strike', it is a connecting phrase of the legatee omitted, as in 'what exceeded' and the like. The conclusion is that the legatee of what exceeds the third, if the heirs do not consent to the bequest, does not take from the third to the extent of his share of the whole on the estimate of consent, but rather he and the legatee of the third are equal according to the greatest (Abu Hanifa). As in al-Kusajiyya.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of bequests regarding the division of the third when multiple bequests are made and the heirs do not consent. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The text first states the basic ruling: if someone bequeaths one-third to Zayd and another similar amount to another, and the heirs do not consent, the third is divided in half between them by agreement. If he bequeaths one-third to Zayd and one-sixth to another, the third is divided in thirds (two-thirds of the third to Zayd, one-third to the other) by agreement. If he bequeaths one-third to Bakr and the whole of his wealth to another, Abu Hanifa says the third is divided in half between them (i.e., each gets half of the third), while the two companions say it should be divided into fourths (i.e., Bakr gets one-fourth of the third, the other gets three-fourths). The commentary then explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa considers that a bequest exceeding the third is entirely void if the heirs do not consent; thus the legatee of the whole is treated as if he were bequeathed only one-third, so they share equally. The two companions hold that only the excess over the third is void, so the legatee of the whole is entitled to a share in the third proportional to his full bequest. The passage further discusses the calculation methods when the heirs do consent, and the famous principle 'the legatee is not struck with more than the third' (لا يضرب الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث). This means that under Abu Hanifa's view, a legatee of more than a third does not 'strike' (i.e., get a share) in the third beyond the amount that makes his bequest equal to a third; he and the legatee of one-third share equally. The commentary uses arithmetic examples to illustrate the division of shares. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two companions, as indicated by the later references like Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
الضرب (al-darb): A technical arithmetic term meaning the allocation of shares by multiplying the legatee's proportional share in the bequest by the available third of the estate.
الوصية بالثلث (al-wasiyyah bi al-thuluth): A bequest of one-third of the testator's wealth, which is the maximum amount that can be bequeathed without the consent of the heirs.
إجازة الورثة (ijazat al-wurathah): The consent of the heirs after the testator's death to allow a bequest exceeding one-third.
المنازعة (al-munaza'ah): Mutual claim or dispute; a method of dividing the third when two legatees both claim a share in it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Bakr and the whole of his wealth to 'Amr, and the heirs do not consent, how does the third get divided according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The third is divided equally between Bakr and 'Amr (each gets half of the third).
B) Bakr gets one-fourth of the third, 'Amr gets three-fourths of the third.
C) 'Amr gets nothing from the third because his bequest is void.
D) The third is divided into sixths: Bakr gets one-sixth, 'Amr gets five-sixths.

Key Takeaway
When heirs do not consent, Abu Hanifa divides the third equally among all legatees of one-third, while the Sahibayn divide it proportionally to the full bequests, and the later school adopts the Sahibayn's view as mufta bihi.

Dispute on Dividing the One-Third Among Multiple Legatees
Explaining the method of dividing the one-third when bequests exceed it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on dividing the one-third when bequests exceed one-third and CALCULATE the resulting shares for each method.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa divides the one-third equally; the Sahibayn divide proportionally based on the size of each bequest.

When a testator bequeaths more than one-third of his estate to multiple legatees and the heirs do not approve, the one-third must be divided among the legatees. But how? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions differed on the method, leading to different outcomes. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the arithmetic behind each view.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the dispute
A testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to Zayd and the entire estate (more than one-third) to 'Amr. Heirs do not approve. The one-third is the only available fund. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on distribution.
The testator's will is interpreted as giving a share of the one-third to each legatee.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and calculation
Abu Hanifa says: the one-third is divided equally between the two legatees, as if each was bequeathed one-third. Therefore each receives half of one-third, i.e., one-sixth of the total estate.
He treats the bequests as competing equally for the one-third.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position and calculation
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: the excess over one-third is void, but the size of each bequest determines the share of the one-third. They treat the bequests proportionally: one-third bequest = 1 share, whole estate = 3 shares, total 4 shares. The one-third is divided into 4 parts: Zayd gets 1/4 of one-third (1/12 of estate), 'Amr gets 3/4 of one-third (1/4 of estate).
They consider the extra bequest as giving a larger claim within the one-third.
4
Analyse the key difference in principle
Abu Hanifa views the testator's intention as giving each legatee a share of the one-third equally, ignoring the excess. The Sahibayn give weight to the excess portion in determining the proportion within the one-third.
The text does not provide a direct rebuttal; it simply presents both methods.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, both legatees get 1/6 each. Under the Sahibayn, Zayd gets 1/12 and 'Amr gets 1/4. The difference is significant.
The mufta bihi position according to later authorities is Abu Hanifa's view.

[ 1 ] قوله : وعندهما سهام الوصية أربعة ... الخ ؛ وعلى هذا الخلاف: لو أوصى لرجل بعبد قيمته مثل ثلث ماله ، ولآخر بعبد قيمته مثل نصف ماله مثلاً، وتمامه في التاتارخانية من الخامس. ولو أوصى لرجل بسيف قيمته مثل سدس ماله ولآخر بسدس ماله، وماله سوى السيف خمسمئة ، فللثاني سدسُها، وللأوّل خمسة أسداس السيف، وسدس السيف بينهما ؛ لأن منازعتهما في سدس السيف فقط، فينصف بينهما، وهذا عند الإمام، وتمام الكلام في «المجمع» وشروحه. كذا في «الرد المحتار»(۲). And the legatee is not given more than one-third according to Abu Hanifa, for it is as if he bequeathed one-third to each, so the one-third is divided in half between them. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Only the excess over one-third is void, meaning that the legatee does not deserve it as a right against the heirs, but it is considered that the legatee takes from the one-third according to the share of that excess, since there is no cause to void this meaning. So the one-third became three, then one-third is one, and the whole became three, making four, so the one-third is divided according to these shares. This is based on a fundamental difference between them, and it is his statement: 'And the legatee is not given more than one-third according to Abu Hanifa.' What is meant by 'giving' is the technical term among accountants: when he bequeaths one-third and the whole, according to Abu Hanifa he has two shares of the bequest, for each one half, then he multiplies half by one-third of the property, so half of one-third is one-sixth, so each gets one-sixth of the property. And according to them, the shares of the bequest are four: for the one with one-third, one, and one out of four is one-quarter, so he multiplies one-quarter by one-third of the property, so one-quarter of one-third is one-quarter of one-third. Then for the one with the whole, three out of four, which is three-quarters, so he multiplies three-quarters by one-third: meaning three-quarters of one-third. And for the one with one-third, one out of four, so he multiplies one by one-third, which is one-quarter, meaning one-quarter of one-third. This is the meaning of multiplication, and many scholars have been perplexed by it. Except in the case of 'muhabah' (favoritism), 'si'ayah' (effort), and 'darahim mursalah' (sent dirhams). Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of distributing the one-third of the estate when a testator makes bequests that exceed one-third and the heirs do not approve. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if someone bequeaths one-third of his estate to one person and the entire estate (or more than one-third) to another, the one-third is divided equally between them, as if he had bequeathed one-third to each. So each gets half of the one-third, i.e., one-sixth of the total estate. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they say the excess over one-third is void (since the heirs do not approve), but the legatee with the larger bequest still has a claim to the one-third according to the proportion of his bequest. They calculate by considering the total shares: the bequest of one-third gives 1 share, the bequest of the whole gives 3 shares (since the whole is three times one-third), making 4 shares in total. The one-third is then divided into 4 parts: the legatee with one-third gets 1/4 of the one-third (i.e., 1/12 of the estate), and the legatee with the whole gets 3/4 of the one-third (i.e., 3/12 or 1/4 of the estate). The text then notes that this method of 'multiplying' (ضرب) refers to the arithmetical operation of multiplying shares. The passage then mentions an exception: the ruling that the legatee is not given more than one-third does not apply in cases of muhabah (favoritism in sale), si'ayah (solicitation of the deceased's slaves), and darahim mursalah (loose dirhams left in the estate). The commentary elaborates on the meaning of muhabah and provides additional examples from other works.

Key Terms
ضرب (darb): Technical term meaning 'to allocate a share by multiplying', specifically the arithmetical operation of multiplying the share fraction by the one-third.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by the testator (musi) for the benefit of another after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs approve.
محاباة (muhabah): Favoritism in a transaction, where the deceased sold something below market value to give benefit; it is treated as a bequest from the one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Zayd gets 1/6, 'Amr gets 1/6
B) Zayd gets 1/12, 'Amr gets 1/4
C) Zayd gets 1/3, 'Amr gets nothing
D) Zayd gets 1/4, 'Amr gets 3/4

Key Takeaway
When bequests exceed one-third and heirs do not approve, Abu Hanifa divides the one-third equally among all legatees; this is the relied-upon position.

Exceptions to the Bequest Limit: المحاباة and السعاية
Explains exceptions to the one-third bequest limit with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the one-third bequest limit does not apply in Hanafi law and calculate proportional distribution of the one-third in cases of muḥābāh and si‘āyah.

Core Idea
In muḥābāh and si‘āyah, legatees take proportionally from the one-third even if their individual bequest exceeds one-third.

In Hanafi inheritance law, bequests cannot exceed one-third of the estate unless heirs consent. However, certain transactions are exempt because they are not pure bequests but sales or emancipation mechanisms. This lesson explores two such exceptions—muḥābāh (a favorable sale) and si‘āyah (a slave's effort to earn freedom)—and explains how the one-third is divided proportionally among the beneficiaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recall that bequests are limited to one-third of the estate; if multiple bequests exceed one-third, they are reduced proportionally.
This is the baseline rule from which the exceptions depart.
2
Recognize the Exception
In muḥābāh and si‘āyah, the bequest (discount or freedom portion) is taken from the one-third according to its size, even if that bequest alone exceeds one-third. The transaction remains valid and the estate is not voided.
The exception is based on the nature of the transaction (sale or emancipation) rather than a pure gift.
3
Analyze the Muḥābāh Example
Work through the given example: two slaves worth 30 and 60, sold to Zayd at 10 and to 'Amr at 20. The bequest for Zayd is 20, for 'Amr is 40. The one-third of total estate (90) is 30. Divide 30 into thirds: Zayd gets 10, 'Amr gets 20. 'Amr takes 20 from the one-third, even though his bequest (40) exceeds 30.
The sale prices are adjusted so that the bequest portion is taken from the one-third.
4
Analyze the Si‘āyah Example
Two slaves emancipated in a will, values 30 and 60, no other assets. Bequest shares: first slave one-third of estate, second two-thirds. The one-third (30) is divided accordingly: first gets 10 (one-third of 30) and is freed for 10, must earn 20; second gets 20 (two-thirds of 30) and is freed for 20, must earn 40.
Each slave takes according to his bequest from the one-third, even if the emancipation value exceeds one-third.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dimension
Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) agree on the exception here, though they differ on the calculation method in other cases of multiple bequests.
This agreement is a point of fiqh harmony within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا في المحاباة والسعاية والدراهم المرسلة) ، صورة المحاباة : أن يكون للرجل عبدان قيمة أحدهما ثلاثون، والآخر ستُون، فأوصى بأن يباع الأول من زيد بعشرة، والآخر من عمر و بعشرين، ولا مال له سواهما، فالوصية في حق زيد بعشرين، وفي حق عمرو بأربعين ، يقسم الثلث بينهما أثلاثاً فيباعُ الأول من زيد بعشرين، والعشرة وصية له، ويباعُ الثَّاني من عمرو بأربعين، والعشرون وصية له، فأخذ عمرو من الثَّلُثِ بقدر وصيته، وإن كانت زائدة على الثلث. وصورة السعاية : أعتق عبدين قيمتهما ما ذكر، ولا مال له سواهما، فالوصية للأوَّلِ بثلث المال والثاني بثلثي المال، فسهام الوصية بينهما أثلاث، واحد للأول ، واثنان للثاني ، فيقسم الثلث بينهما كذلك، فيعتق من الأول ثلاثة ، وهو عشرة، ويسعي في عشرين، ويعتق من الثَّاني ثُلُثَه، وهو عشرون، ويسعى في أربعين، فيضرب كل بقدر وصيَّته وإن كان زائداً على الثلث.
Except in the case of المحاباة (favorable sale), السعاية (earning freedom), and الدراهم المرسلة (loose dirhams). The example of المحاباة is that a man has two slaves, one worth thirty and the other sixty, and he wills that the first be sold to Zayd for ten and the second to 'Amr for twenty, and he has no other property. So the bequest for Zayd is twenty and for 'Amr is forty. The one-third is divided between them in thirds: the first is sold to Zayd for twenty, of which ten is a bequest for him, and the second is sold to 'Amr for forty, of which twenty is a bequest for him. So 'Amr takes from the one-third according to his bequest, even though it exceeds the one-third. The example of السعاية: He emancipates two slaves worth the same amounts, and he has no other property. So the bequest for the first is one-third of the estate and for the second two-thirds. The shares of the bequest between them are thirds: one for the first and two for the second. Thus, the one-third is divided between them accordingly. So from the first, one-third is emancipated — which is ten — and he earns freedom for twenty; from the second, one-third is emancipated — which is twenty — and he earns freedom for forty. So each takes according to his bequest, even if it exceeds the one-third.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rule that normally, a legatee cannot take more than one-third of the estate if the bequests exceed that limit, except in three cases: المحاباة (a favorable sale), السعاية (where a slave earns freedom by working), and الدراهم المرسلة (loose dirhams). The author provides concrete examples. In المحاباة, a terminally ill person sells slaves below market value, and the difference is a bequest. Here, each buyer receives the full discount amount from the one-third, even if it exceeds the one-third, because the transaction is a sale not a pure bequest. In السعاية, a master emancipates slaves in a will, and the slaves then work to pay off their value. Again, each slave is freed proportionally and must earn the remainder. The calculation shows that the bequest shares are divided proportionally from the one-third, and each takes according to their due, even if that share exceeds the one-third. This is an exception to the general rule that no bequest can exceed one-third of the estate. The passage implies an intra-Hanafi dispute, as the calculation method differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in other cases, but here all agree on the exception.

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): A favor or discount in a sale, where a seller sells below market value; the difference is considered a bequest.
سعاية (si‘āyah): The slave's effort to earn freedom by working and paying off his value; used in the context of emancipation by will.
ضرب (ḍarb): Multiplication in arithmetic; here it means calculating the share of the bequest from the one-third.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum that can be allocated to bequests without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of muḥābāh from this lesson, how much does 'Amr receive from the one-third of the estate?
A) 10
B) 20
C) 30
D) 40

Key Takeaway
In muḥābāh and si‘āyah, even if an individual bequest exceeds one-third of the estate, the beneficiary receives only a proportional share of the one-third based on the total bequests.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Successive Bequests: Absorption of One-Sixth into One-Third
Clarifying the absorption of one-sixth into one-third in successive bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a testator bequeaths one-sixth then one-third to the same person, and explain the effect of heirs' consent.

Core Idea
A later larger bequest absorbs an earlier smaller one; the legatee receives one-third total, not half.

When a testator makes two successive bequests to the same person—first one-sixth, later one-third—the later, larger bequest includes the earlier one. The legatee receives one-third of the estate, even if the heirs consent, because their consent confirms the bequest but does not create an additional one-sixth. This principle avoids exceeding the one-third limit and respects the testator's probable intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two bequests and their order
The testator first says: 'One-sixth of my wealth is for Zaid.' Later he says: 'One-third of my wealth is for Zaid.' The later bequest is larger and includes one-sixth.
The order matters: the later bequest replaces or subsumes the earlier.
2
Apply the absorption principle
The one-sixth is included within the one-third. The legatee does not accumulate both; he gets only one-third total because the larger share already contains the smaller.
This is based on the Hanafi rule that a bequest cannot exceed one-third without heirs' consent; here the total is one-third, so no consent is needed (though heirs may still consent).
3
Understand the role of heirs' consent
If the heirs consent, the legatee still gets only one-third. Their consent does not create an additional grant; it merely ratifies the bequest of one-third. The one-sixth is not added separately.
The qualifier 'if they consented' in the original passage is precautionary: it prevents the misunderstanding that without consent the legatee gets half.
4
Recognize the logical problem and its resolution
One might object: the second statement 'one-third is for him' cannot be informative (false) so must be creative, giving half. The resolution: the second bequest is an inclusive grant, not an additional one. It is interpreted as 'the one-third that includes the one-sixth'.
This interpretation is consistent with the Muslim testator's good faith: he likely intended the one-third to replace the earlier one-sixth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : سدس مالي له ، ثُمَّ قال : ثلثه له ، وأجازوا، له ثلث : أي يكون السُّدُسُ داخلاً في الثلث، فإن قلت : قولُهُ: ثُلُثُ مالي له ؛ إن كان إخباراً فكاذب، وان كان إنشاء يجب أن يكون له النِّصْفُ عند إجازة الورثة ، وإن كان في السدس إخبار وفي السدس إنشاء ، فهذا ممتنع أيضاً.
قال في «الهداية»: ومن أوصى بسهم من ماله فله أحسن سهام الورثة إلا أن ينقص عن السدس ، فيتم له السدس، ولا يزاد عليه مآل المصنف به وصاحب «الهداية» واحد، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له.
وقالا : له مثل نصيب أحد الورثة الذي له أقلّ الأنصباء، ولا يزاد على الثلث إلا أن تجيز الورثة ؛ لأنّ السهم يراد به أحد سهام الورثة عرفاً، لا سيما في الوصية، والأقل متيقن به فيصرفُ إليه إلا إذا زاد على الثلث فيرد عليه ؛ لأنه لا مزيد عليه عند عدم الإجارة.
وله : إن السهم هو السدس، هو المروي عن ابن مسعود ، وقد رفعه إلى النبي فيما يروى ؛ ولأنه يذكر ويراد به السدس، فإن إياسا له قال : السهم في اللغة عبارة عن السدس، ويذكر ويراد به سهم من سهام الورثة فيعطى ما ذكرنا انتهى [١] قوله : له ثلث ؛ قال صاحب (رد المحتار » (۳) : «أقول : حاصل السؤال أنّ قولَ الموصي : ثلث مالي له لا يصلح إخباراً ؛ لأنه كذب، فتعين الإنشاء، فينبغي أن يكون له النصف ؛ لأنّ عموم السدس والثلث النصف والربع أنا سلّمنا أن قوله : سدس مالي له يحتمل أن يكون المراد به زيادة سدس أو ثلثاً آخر غير السدس المذكور، فيحمل على المتيقن.
وبقي هاهنا شيء، وهو أنه لا يخلو من أن يكون الثلث الذي أجازه الورثة ثلثاً زائداً على السدس الذي أجازوه ؛ أو لا يكون ثلثاً زائداً عليه، أو لا وجه لإجازتهم بلا تعيين المراد، إذ مرجعه إلى إجازة اللفظ ، ولا معنى له والثاني يأباه قوله : وأجازوا ؛ لأنه مستغن عن إجازتهم، وعلى الأول لا يصح الجواب المذكور.
قلت : لا جواب لهذا السؤال.
ولعله لذلك أسقط صاحب «الكنز» القيد المذكور، والجواب أن هذا القيد غير احترازي بل ذكروه؛ لئلا يتوهّم أنّ له النصف عند الإجازة، ويفهم أنّ له الثلث عند عدم الإجازة بالطريق الأولى. لكن بقى هاهنا إشكال ذكره في «الشرنبلالية»، ونقل نحوه عن قاضي زاده : وهو أن صاحب الحق رضي بما يحتمله كلامُ الموصي من اجتماع الثلث مع السدس ، وامتناعُ ما كان غير متيقن لحق الوارث ، فبعد الرضا كيف يتكلف للمنع ...اهـ. وجوابه : أنه لما احتمله كلامُ الموصي حملناه على المتيقن الذي يملكه وهو الوصية بالثلث كما مرّ، والوصيّة إيجاب تمليك، فكان إيجاب الثلث متيقنا، وإيجاب الزائد مشكوكاً فيه وإجازة الوارث لا تعمل إلا فيما أوجبه الموصى، ولم نتيقن بإيجاب فيما زاد على الثلث حتى تعمل الإجازة عملها، فلغت ؛ لأنَّ الإجازة ليست ابتداءً تمليك ، وإنّما هي تنفيذ لعقد الموصي المتوقف عليها ؛ ولهذا يثبت الملك للمجاز له من قبل الموصي ، لا من قبل المجيز، كما ع». هذا خلاصة ما في رد المحتار). سيجي [١] قوله : قلت ؛ هكذا في النسخ، بلا ذكر حجاب، بل مع بياض بعد قوله : قلت، فلم يعلل كذب الإخبار في ثلث مالي، وفي سدس مالي، ووجهه : أنه أضاف الكل إلى نفسه، والإخبار بأنّ ماله لغيره كاذب.
ولعل الجواب هو أنه إنشاء ، لكن لو لم يكن السدس داخلاً في الثلث لزم الوصية بما زاد على الثلث ؛ وهو لا يجوز على ما سبق، فهذا يكون دليلا على أن الموصي المسلم أراد الدخول في الثلث حملاً لحال المسلم على ما هو اللائق به، فإنّه قال له : من مالي ما زاد على السدس في الثلث، وفي هذا الثلث فقط سواء كان أجازت الورثة أو لم يجيزوا.
فقوله له أجازت الورثة؛ لبيان أنه لو لم يجز الورثة له الثلث فقط بالطريق الأولى، هذا تقرير شيخ الإسلام له في هذا المقام.
If he said: ‘One-sixth of my wealth is for him,’ then said: ‘One-third of his wealth is for him,’ and they consented, he has one-third: meaning that the one-sixth is included within the one-third. If you say: his statement ‘One-third of my wealth is for him’ if it is informative, then it is false; and if it is creative, then at the time of the heirs’ consent he should have half. And if part of the ‘one-sixth’ is informative and part creative, this is also impossible.
[Al-Hidayah] said: Whoever makes a bequest of a share (sahm) of his wealth, then he gets the best share of the heirs, unless it falls short of one-sixth, then it is completed to one-sixth, and no more is added. The final outcome of the author and the author of Al-Hidayah is the same. This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.
The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He gets the share of one of the heirs who has the smallest portion, and it is not increased beyond one-third unless the heirs consent. Because the term ‘share’ (sahm) in customary usage refers to one of the shares of the heirs, especially in bequests. The smallest is certain, so it is directed to that, unless it exceeds one-third, then it is reduced to one-third, because there is no increase beyond it without consent.
His (Abu Hanifa’s) proof: That ‘share’ is one-sixth. That is reported from Ibn Mas'ud, and he raised it to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in what is narrated; and because it is mentioned and by it is meant one-sixth. Iyas stated that ‘share’ in the language is an expression for one-sixth. And it is mentioned and by it is meant a share of the shares of the heirs, so he is given what we mentioned. End.
[Commentary]: The author of Radd al-Muhtar said: I say: The gist of the question is that the testator’s statement ‘one-third of my wealth is for him’ cannot be informative because it is false; so it must be creative, and it should be half; because the sum of one-sixth and one-third is half. But we concede that his statement ‘one-sixth of my wealth is for him’ could mean an additional one-sixth or a one-third other than the mentioned one-sixth, so it is interpreted according to the certain.
There remains an issue here: It is unavoidable that the one-third which the heirs consented to is either an additional one-third beyond the one-sixth which they consented to, or it is not additional. There is no basis for their consent without specifying the intended meaning, because it comes down to consent of the wording, which has no meaning. The second possibility is rejected by his statement “and they consented” because it would be independent of their consent. On the first possibility, the mentioned response is invalid.
I said: There is no answer to this question.
Perhaps for this reason the author of al-Kanz omitted the mentioned qualifier. The answer is that this qualifier is not restrictive; rather they mentioned it to prevent the misunderstanding that he gets half upon consent, and it is understood that he gets one-third without consent by primary implication. But there remains an objection mentioned in al-Sharnabalaliyya, and similar was transmitted from Qadizadeh: that the right-holder (the legatee) consented to what the testator’s speech could bear—the combination of one-third with one-sixth—and prevention of what is not certain for the heir. So after consent, why is prevention carried out with difficulty? The answer: Since the testator’s speech bore that, we interpret it according to the certain thing he possesses, which is the bequest of one-third as passed. The bequest is a grant of ownership, so granting the one-third is certain, and granting the excess is doubtful. The heir’s consent operates only on what the testator granted, and we are not certain of the grant regarding what is beyond one-third for the consent to take effect. So it is null. Because consent is not an initial grant; rather it is a ratification of the testator’s contract which depends on it. For this reason, ownership unfolds for the grantee from the testator, not from the ratifier, as is known. This is the summary from Radd al-Muhtar.
[Commentary]: The word ‘I said’: it appears in manuscripts without mention of a reason, but with blank after ‘I said’. Thus it does not explain the falsity of the informative statement in ‘one-third of my wealth’ and ‘one-sixth of my wealth’. The reason: he attributed the entirety to himself, and informing that his wealth belongs to others is false.
Perhaps the answer is that it is a creative statement, but if the one-sixth were not included in the one-third, the bequest would exceed one-third, which is not permissible as previously established. This is evidence that the Muslim testator intended inclusion in the one-third, interpreting the Muslim’s state according to what is befitting. So he says: From my wealth, what exceeds the one-sixth falls within the one-third, and within that one-third only, whether the heirs consent or not.
His statement ‘if the heirs consented’ is to clarify that even if the heirs had not consented, he would take only the one-third by primary implication. This is the explanation of Shaykh al-Islam on this point.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific case in Hanafi inheritance law: a testator first bequeaths one-sixth of his wealth to a person, then later bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the same person. The question is: how do these bequests combine, especially if the heirs consent? The ruling is that the one-sixth is absorbed into the one-third, so the legatee receives only one-third total. This is because the later bequest (one-third) is larger and includes the earlier one-sixth. The author clarifies that this ruling applies when the heirs consent; if they do not, the legatee still gets one-third (and not half) because the one-third is the certain amount, and any additional bequest is uncertain. There is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa holds that the term 'sahm' (share) in a bequest means one-sixth, based on a hadith and linguistic evidence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it means the smallest share of any heir, but cannot exceed one-third without heirs' consent. The text then engages with a logical question: the testator's second statement 'one-third of my wealth is for him' cannot be informative (it would be false) and must be creative, but then the legatee should get half (sum of one-sixth and one-third) upon consent. The commentator resolves this by interpreting the second statement as an inclusive grant, not an additional one. The consent of the heirs confirms the one-third, not the creation of a new bequest. The passage concludes by explaining why the qualifier 'if they consented' is not restrictive but precautionary, and addresses an objection from later scholars.

Key Terms
سدس (suds): One-sixth of the estate.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum bequeatable without heirs' consent.
إجازة (ijazah): Consent of the heirs after the testator's death to validate a bequest exceeding one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One-sixth only
B) One-third only
C) Half (one-sixth plus one-third)
D) One-sixth plus one-third, totaling five-sixths

Key Takeaway
A later larger bequest absorbs an earlier smaller bequest to the same person; the legatee receives only the larger amount, up to one-third.

The Meaning of 'Sahm' in Bequests: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'sahm' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on the meaning of 'sahm' (share) in a bequest and evaluate their proofs.

Core Idea
The term 'sahm' is ambiguous: Abu Hanifa interprets it as one-sixth; the Sahibayn as the smallest heir's share.

When a testator bequeaths 'a share' (sahm) of his wealth, what exactly does the legatee receive? The Hanafi school has two views. Abu Hanifa, relying on a hadith and linguistic evidence, holds that 'sahm' means one-sixth. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that customary usage in bequests points to the smallest share of any heir. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the context of the dispute
The dispute arises when a testator uses the word 'sahm' (share) without specifying a fraction. The ruling affects how much the legatee receives.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa: The legatee gets the best share of the heirs (the highest portion), but if that is less than one-sixth, it is raised to one-sixth, and no more is added. His proof: a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (marfu') that 'sahm' means one-sixth, and a linguistic statement from Iyas that 'sahm' in Arabic is one-sixth.
The hadith is a strong evidence, but its chain is zanni.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn: The legatee gets the smallest share of the heirs. Their proof: customary usage ('urf) — in bequests, 'sahm' is understood as one of the shares of the heirs. The smallest is the certain amount. However, it cannot exceed one-third without heirs' consent.
The Sahibayn rely on 'urf over linguistic meaning.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the legatee could get a large share (e.g., half) if one heir's share is half, subject to the one-third cap? Actually the text says 'no more is added' — meaning not beyond the best share? It seems Abu Hanifa does not explicitly cap at one-third in this context, but the general one-third rule applies. Under the Sahibayn, the legatee gets the smallest share, which is less, but capped at one-third. The practical difference is thus the base amount before the cap.
In typical cases with heirs having shares like 1/2, 1/3, 1/6, the smallest share is 1/6, so both views give 1/6 if no cap. If the smallest is less than 1/6, Sahibayn give that less, while Abu Hanifa gives 1/6. If the best share is 1/2, Abu Hanifa gives 1/2 (but then the one-third cap might reduce it).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The passage does not give an explicit tarjih. However, later scholars tend to follow the Sahibayn's view in fatwa because it is more cautious and aligns with 'urf. But the absorption principle in the successive bequests case is unaffected.
The mufta bihi for the meaning of 'sahm' is the Sahibayn's view according to many later Hanafi authorities.

فإن قال : سدس مالي له ، ثُمَّ قال : ثلثه له ، وأجازوا، له ثلث : أي يكون السُّدُسُ داخلاً في الثلث، فإن قلت : قولُهُ: ثُلُثُ مالي له ؛ إن كان إخباراً فكاذب، وان كان إنشاء يجب أن يكون له النِّصْفُ عند إجازة الورثة ، وإن كان في السدس إخبار وفي السدس إنشاء ، فهذا ممتنع أيضاً.
قال في «الهداية»: ومن أوصى بسهم من ماله فله أحسن سهام الورثة إلا أن ينقص عن السدس ، فيتم له السدس، ولا يزاد عليه مآل المصنف به وصاحب «الهداية» واحد، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له.
وقالا : له مثل نصيب أحد الورثة الذي له أقلّ الأنصباء، ولا يزاد على الثلث إلا أن تجيز الورثة ؛ لأنّ السهم يراد به أحد سهام الورثة عرفاً، لا سيما في الوصية، والأقل متيقن به فيصرفُ إليه إلا إذا زاد على الثلث فيرد عليه ؛ لأنه لا مزيد عليه عند عدم الإجارة.
وله : إن السهم هو السدس، هو المروي عن ابن مسعود ، وقد رفعه إلى النبي فيما يروى ؛ ولأنه يذكر ويراد به السدس، فإن إياسا له قال : السهم في اللغة عبارة عن السدس، ويذكر ويراد به سهم من سهام الورثة فيعطى ما ذكرنا انتهى [١] قوله : له ثلث ؛ قال صاحب (رد المحتار » (۳) : «أقول : حاصل السؤال أنّ قولَ الموصي : ثلث مالي له لا يصلح إخباراً ؛ لأنه كذب، فتعين الإنشاء، فينبغي أن يكون له النصف ؛ لأنّ عموم السدس والثلث النصف والربع أنا سلّمنا أن قوله : سدس مالي له يحتمل أن يكون المراد به زيادة سدس أو ثلثاً آخر غير السدس المذكور، فيحمل على المتيقن.
وبقي هاهنا شيء، وهو أنه لا يخلو من أن يكون الثلث الذي أجازه الورثة ثلثاً زائداً على السدس الذي أجازوه ؛ أو لا يكون ثلثاً زائداً عليه، أو لا وجه لإجازتهم بلا تعيين المراد، إذ مرجعه إلى إجازة اللفظ ، ولا معنى له والثاني يأباه قوله : وأجازوا ؛ لأنه مستغن عن إجازتهم، وعلى الأول لا يصح الجواب المذكور.
قلت : لا جواب لهذا السؤال.
ولعله لذلك أسقط صاحب «الكنز» القيد المذكور، والجواب أن هذا القيد غير احترازي بل ذكروه؛ لئلا يتوهّم أنّ له النصف عند الإجازة، ويفهم أنّ له الثلث عند عدم الإجازة بالطريق الأولى. لكن بقى هاهنا إشكال ذكره في «الشرنبلالية»، ونقل نحوه عن قاضي زاده : وهو أن صاحب الحق رضي بما يحتمله كلامُ الموصي من اجتماع الثلث مع السدس ، وامتناعُ ما كان غير متيقن لحق الوارث ، فبعد الرضا كيف يتكلف للمنع ...اهـ. وجوابه : أنه لما احتمله كلامُ الموصي حملناه على المتيقن الذي يملكه وهو الوصية بالثلث كما مرّ، والوصيّة إيجاب تمليك، فكان إيجاب الثلث متيقنا، وإيجاب الزائد مشكوكاً فيه وإجازة الوارث لا تعمل إلا فيما أوجبه الموصى، ولم نتيقن بإيجاب فيما زاد على الثلث حتى تعمل الإجازة عملها، فلغت ؛ لأنَّ الإجازة ليست ابتداءً تمليك ، وإنّما هي تنفيذ لعقد الموصي المتوقف عليها ؛ ولهذا يثبت الملك للمجاز له من قبل الموصي ، لا من قبل المجيز، كما ع». هذا خلاصة ما في رد المحتار). سيجي [١] قوله : قلت ؛ هكذا في النسخ، بلا ذكر حجاب، بل مع بياض بعد قوله : قلت، فلم يعلل كذب الإخبار في ثلث مالي، وفي سدس مالي، ووجهه : أنه أضاف الكل إلى نفسه، والإخبار بأنّ ماله لغيره كاذب.
ولعل الجواب هو أنه إنشاء ، لكن لو لم يكن السدس داخلاً في الثلث لزم الوصية بما زاد على الثلث ؛ وهو لا يجوز على ما سبق، فهذا يكون دليلا على أن الموصي المسلم أراد الدخول في الثلث حملاً لحال المسلم على ما هو اللائق به، فإنّه قال له : من مالي ما زاد على السدس في الثلث، وفي هذا الثلث فقط سواء كان أجازت الورثة أو لم يجيزوا.
فقوله له أجازت الورثة؛ لبيان أنه لو لم يجز الورثة له الثلث فقط بالطريق الأولى، هذا تقرير شيخ الإسلام له في هذا المقام.
If he said: ‘One-sixth of my wealth is for him,’ then said: ‘One-third of his wealth is for him,’ and they consented, he has one-third: meaning that the one-sixth is included within the one-third. If you say: his statement ‘One-third of my wealth is for him’ if it is informative, then it is false; and if it is creative, then at the time of the heirs’ consent he should have half. And if part of the ‘one-sixth’ is informative and part creative, this is also impossible.
[Al-Hidayah] said: Whoever makes a bequest of a share (sahm) of his wealth, then he gets the best share of the heirs, unless it falls short of one-sixth, then it is completed to one-sixth, and no more is added. The final outcome of the author and the author of Al-Hidayah is the same. This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.
The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He gets the share of one of the heirs who has the smallest portion, and it is not increased beyond one-third unless the heirs consent. Because the term ‘share’ (sahm) in customary usage refers to one of the shares of the heirs, especially in bequests. The smallest is certain, so it is directed to that, unless it exceeds one-third, then it is reduced to one-third, because there is no increase beyond it without consent.
His (Abu Hanifa’s) proof: That ‘share’ is one-sixth. That is reported from Ibn Mas'ud, and he raised it to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in what is narrated; and because it is mentioned and by it is meant one-sixth. Iyas stated that ‘share’ in the language is an expression for one-sixth. And it is mentioned and by it is meant a share of the shares of the heirs, so he is given what we mentioned. End.
[Commentary]: The author of Radd al-Muhtar said: I say: The gist of the question is that the testator’s statement ‘one-third of my wealth is for him’ cannot be informative because it is false; so it must be creative, and it should be half; because the sum of one-sixth and one-third is half. But we concede that his statement ‘one-sixth of my wealth is for him’ could mean an additional one-sixth or a one-third other than the mentioned one-sixth, so it is interpreted according to the certain.
There remains an issue here: It is unavoidable that the one-third which the heirs consented to is either an additional one-third beyond the one-sixth which they consented to, or it is not additional. There is no basis for their consent without specifying the intended meaning, because it comes down to consent of the wording, which has no meaning. The second possibility is rejected by his statement “and they consented” because it would be independent of their consent. On the first possibility, the mentioned response is invalid.
I said: There is no answer to this question.
Perhaps for this reason the author of al-Kanz omitted the mentioned qualifier. The answer is that this qualifier is not restrictive; rather they mentioned it to prevent the misunderstanding that he gets half upon consent, and it is understood that he gets one-third without consent by primary implication. But there remains an objection mentioned in al-Sharnabalaliyya, and similar was transmitted from Qadizadeh: that the right-holder (the legatee) consented to what the testator’s speech could bear—the combination of one-third with one-sixth—and prevention of what is not certain for the heir. So after consent, why is prevention carried out with difficulty? The answer: Since the testator’s speech bore that, we interpret it according to the certain thing he possesses, which is the bequest of one-third as passed. The bequest is a grant of ownership, so granting the one-third is certain, and granting the excess is doubtful. The heir’s consent operates only on what the testator granted, and we are not certain of the grant regarding what is beyond one-third for the consent to take effect. So it is null. Because consent is not an initial grant; rather it is a ratification of the testator’s contract which depends on it. For this reason, ownership unfolds for the grantee from the testator, not from the ratifier, as is known. This is the summary from Radd al-Muhtar.
[Commentary]: The word ‘I said’: it appears in manuscripts without mention of a reason, but with blank after ‘I said’. Thus it does not explain the falsity of the informative statement in ‘one-third of my wealth’ and ‘one-sixth of my wealth’. The reason: he attributed the entirety to himself, and informing that his wealth belongs to others is false.
Perhaps the answer is that it is a creative statement, but if the one-sixth were not included in the one-third, the bequest would exceed one-third, which is not permissible as previously established. This is evidence that the Muslim testator intended inclusion in the one-third, interpreting the Muslim’s state according to what is befitting. So he says: From my wealth, what exceeds the one-sixth falls within the one-third, and within that one-third only, whether the heirs consent or not.
His statement ‘if the heirs consented’ is to clarify that even if the heirs had not consented, he would take only the one-third by primary implication. This is the explanation of Shaykh al-Islam on this point.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific case in Hanafi inheritance law: a testator first bequeaths one-sixth of his wealth to a person, then later bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the same person. The question is: how do these bequests combine, especially if the heirs consent? The ruling is that the one-sixth is absorbed into the one-third, so the legatee receives only one-third total. This is because the later bequest (one-third) is larger and includes the earlier one-sixth. The author clarifies that this ruling applies when the heirs consent; if they do not, the legatee still gets one-third (and not half) because the one-third is the certain amount, and any additional bequest is uncertain. There is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa holds that the term 'sahm' (share) in a bequest means one-sixth, based on a hadith and linguistic evidence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it means the smallest share of any heir, but cannot exceed one-third without heirs' consent. The text then engages with a logical question: the testator's second statement 'one-third of my wealth is for him' cannot be informative (it would be false) and must be creative, but then the legatee should get half (sum of one-sixth and one-third) upon consent. The commentator resolves this by interpreting the second statement as an inclusive grant, not an additional one. The consent of the heirs confirms the one-third, not the creation of a new bequest. The passage concludes by explaining why the qualifier 'if they consented' is not restrictive but precautionary, and addresses an objection from later scholars.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): A share of the estate; interpreted variously: as one-sixth (Abu Hanifa) or as the share of an heir (Sahibayn).
عرف (urf): Customary usage; a source of law in Hanafi usul, especially in interpreting ambiguous terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a testator bequeaths 'a share' (sahm) and the heirs' shares are: wife 1/8, son 7/8, what does the legatee receive?
A) 1/6
B) 1/8
C) 7/8
D) 1/3

Key Takeaway
The term 'sahm' in bequests is ambiguous; the mufta bihi is that it means the smallest share of any heir, not exceeding one-third.

Ambiguous Bequest: 'A Third and a Sixth' – Hanafi Interpretation
Resolving ambiguity in a bequest wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a bequest stating 'a third and a sixth of my property' gives only one-third in Hanafi fiqh and apply the principles of certainty and validity in interpreting ambiguous wills.

Core Idea
The sixth is included in the third; the legatee receives only one-third.

When a testator's words appear to give two shares, Hanafi jurists apply principles of certainty and restraint: the certain share (third) is upheld, and any excess is doubtful. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the rule that 'a third and a sixth' yields one-third, protecting both the testator's intent and the heirs' rights.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the primary ruling: the legatee receives only a third, not a third plus a sixth. The sixth is considered included within the third.
This interpretation avoids exceeding the one-third limit without heir consent.
2
Identify the opposing interpretation
Some scholars (or hypothetical objectors) read the wording literally as two separate bequests, which would give half the estate.
This literal reading seems to be the natural understanding but leads to an invalid excess.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent relies on the apparent text: 'a third and a sixth' suggests two distinct shares. Any ambiguity should benefit the legatee, especially if heirs consent.
The objection is that after consent, why prevent the combination?
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses the certainty principle: the bequest is a transfer of ownership; only the third is certain. The sixth is doubtful, and the testator's speech is interpreted in a manner consistent with validity (not exceeding one-third). Additionally, the heir's consent only executes what was definitely stipulated; it cannot create a new bequest.
Consent is not a new transfer but execution of the testator's will.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that the opposing view gives half; the Hanafi view gives one-third. This matters for calculating shares and seeking heir consent.
The dispute is resolved in favor of the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت : لا جواب لهذا السؤال.
ولعله لذلك أسقط صاحب «الكنز» القيد المذكور، والجواب أن هذا القيد غير احترازي بل ذكروه؛ لئلا يتوهّم أنّ له النصف عند الإجازة، ويفهم أنّ له الثلث عند عدم الإجازة بالطريق الأولى. لكن بقى هاهنا إشكال ذكره في «الشرنبلالية»، ونقل نحوه عن قاضي زاده : وهو أن صاحب الحق رضي بما يحتمله كلامُ الموصي من اجتماع الثلث مع السدس ، وامتناعُ ما كان غير متيقن لحق الوارث ، فبعد الرضا كيف يتكلف للمنع ...اهـ. وجوابه : أنه لما احتمله كلامُ الموصي حملناه على المتيقن الذي يملكه وهو الوصية بالثلث كما مرّ، والوصيّة إيجاب تمليك، فكان إيجاب الثلث متيقنا، وإيجاب الزائد مشكوكاً فيه وإجازة الوارث لا تعمل إلا فيما أوجبه الموصى، ولم نتيقن بإيجاب فيما زاد على الثلث حتى تعمل الإجازة عملها، فلغت ؛ لأنَّ الإجازة ليست ابتداءً تمليك ، وإنّما هي تنفيذ لعقد الموصي المتوقف عليها ؛ ولهذا يثبت الملك للمجاز له من قبل الموصي ، لا من قبل المجيز، كما ع». هذا خلاصة ما في رد المحتار). سيجي [١] قوله : قلت ; هكذا في النسخ، بلا ذكر حجاب، بل مع بياض بعد قوله : قلت، فلم يعلل كذب الإخبار في ثلث مالي، وفي سدس مالي، ووجهه : أنه أضاف الكل إلى نفسه، والإخبار بأنّ ماله لغيره كاذب.
ولعل الجواب هو أنه إنشاء ، لكن لو لم يكن السدس داخلاً في الثلث لزم الوصية بما زاد على الثلث ; وهو لا يجوز على ما سبق، فهذا يكون دليلا على أن الموصي المسلم أراد الدخول في الثلث حملاً لحال المسلم على ما هو اللائق به، فإنّه قال له : من مالي ما زاد على السدس في الثلث، وفي هذا الثلث فقط سواء كان أجازت الورثة أو لم يجيزوا.
فقوله له أجازت الورثة; لبيان أنه لو لم يجز الورثة له الثلث فقط بالطريق الأولى، هذا تقرير شيخ الإسلام له في هذا المقام.
(۱) رد المحتار (٦ : ٦٧١).
I said: There is no answer to this question. Perhaps because of this the author of al-Kanz dropped the mentioned condition. The answer is that this condition is not exclusive but they mentioned it to prevent the misunderstanding that he gets half upon consent, and it is understood that he gets the third without consent by way of priority. But there remains an issue mentioned in al-Sharnablaliyya, and similar was transmitted from Qadizadeh: that the right-holder (heir) consented to what the testator's speech could imply – the combination of the third and the sixth – and the prevention of what was not certain regarding the heir's right. So after consent, why trouble to prevent... etc. Its answer: Since the testator's speech could imply that, we interpreted it as the certain thing he owns, which is the bequest of a third as previously. The bequest is a positive transfer of ownership, so the stipulation of the third is certain, and the stipulation of the excess is doubtful. The heir's consent only operates on what the testator stipulated. We are not certain of stipulation beyond the third for the consent to operate, so it is void because consent is not an initial transfer of ownership but execution of the testator's contract that depends on it. Hence ownership is established for the legatee from the testator, not from the consenting heir, as stated. This is the summary from Radd al-Muhtar. There follows [1] His statement: I said; thus in the copies, without mention of exclusion, but with a blank after his statement: I said. Thus he did not justify the falsity of the statement in 'a third of my property' and 'a sixth of my property'. Its explanation: He attributed it all to himself, and the statement that his property belongs to others is false. Perhaps the answer is that it is a declaration, but if the sixth were not included in the third, it would necessitate a bequest exceeding the third, which is not permissible as previously. This is evidence that the Muslim testator intended inclusion within the third, interpreting the Muslim's state in a manner befitting him, for he said to him: 'from my property, what exceeds the sixth is in the third, and only this third, whether the heirs consent or not.' So his statement 'if the heirs consent' is to clarify that if the heirs do not consent, he gets only the third, by way of priority. This is the determination of Shaykh al-Islam in this regard. (1) Radd al-Muhtar (6:671).
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of an ambiguous bequest. It begins with a reply to an objection: why did the author of al-Kanz drop a certain condition? The answer is that the condition was not meant to be exclusive but to prevent misunderstanding. Then a problem from al-Sharnablaliyya and Qadizadeh is raised: if the heir consents to the possible meaning of the testator's words, why still prevent the combination? The response explains that we take the certain amount (the third) because the will is a transfer of ownership; any addition beyond the third is doubtful and the heir's consent only confirms what is definitely stipulated. The consent cannot create new ownership. Finally, another interpretation is suggested: the statement is a declaration, and if the sixth were not included, it would exceed the third which is invalid, so we assume the testator intended inclusion. This shows the Hanafi method of resolving ambiguous wills in favor of validity and within the one-third limit.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will, an act of donating property after death.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum for a bequest without heir consent.
السدس (al-suds): One-sixth; in this context, alleged additional share.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): The consent of the heirs to a bequest exceeding one-third.
التمليك (al-tamlik): Transfer of ownership, the legal nature of a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a testator says 'I give a third of my property and a sixth of my property' to one person, how much does the legatee receive?
A) One-third
B) One-sixth
C) One-half
D) Two-thirds

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an ambiguous bequest mentioning both a third and a sixth is interpreted as a single bequest of one-third to avoid exceeding the permissible limit.
