Repeating 'في سدس مالي': The Linguistic Rule of Definite Nouns
Linguistic rule for repeated definite bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic rule that repeating a definite noun as definite indicates the same referent in interpreting bequests.

Core Idea
Repeating 'a sixth of my property' twice gives one sixth, not two sixths.

In this passage, we learn a subtle linguistic rule: when a testator repeats a definite noun like 'السدس' (the sixth), the second mention refers to the same sixth, not a second one. This is a general Arabic language principle that Hanafi jurists apply to bequests. We will explore why this rule is default and when exceptions occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase
The testator says 'في سدس مالي' twice in his will. Recognize that the phrase is repeated as a definite noun.
2
State the linguistic principle
The rule: when a definite noun is repeated as definite, the second occurrence refers to the same entity as the first.
This is the default unless evidence indicates otherwise.
3
Apply to bequest
Therefore, the legatee receives only one sixth of the estate, not two sixths.
4
Note the exception
If evidence (qarina) shows the testator intended a different sixth, the second could refer to a different object. Example from Quran: 'the Book' in Surah al-Ma'idah 5:48.
The exception is rare; default is unity.
5
Conclude the ruling
The bequest is valid and executed as a single sixth.
This is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
وفي سدس مالي مكرراً ، له سدس؛ لأنَّ المعرفة إذا أعيدت معرفة كان الثاني عين الأول.
وبثُلُثِ دراهمه ، أو غنمه ، أو ثيابه متفاوتة، أو عبيده إن هلك ثلثاه فله ما بقي في الأولين وثلث الباقي في الآخرين، هذا عندنا وعند زُفَرَه ثُلُثُ الباقي في كل الصور ; لأن حق الموصى له شائع في الجميع، فإذا هَلَكَ ثُلث المال هَلَكَ ثلثا حق الموصى له لنا : أنّ حق الموصى له مقدم على حق الورثة ، فكل ما يجري فيه الجبر على القسمة، ويمكنُ جَمْعُ حق أحد المستحقين في الواحد :
[1] قوله : كان الثاني عين الأوّل ; وهو الأعم الأغلب في اللغة، أما إذا دل الدليل على أنه أريد بالثاني غير الأول لم يكن عينه إذا كما في قوله : وَأَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الْكِتَبَ بِالْحَقِّ مُصَدِّقًا لِمَا بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ مِنَ الْكِتَب (1). كذا في «الكفاية».
[2] قوله : إن هلك ثلثاه ; أي ثلثا الدراهم أو الغنم، بأن كانت ثلاثة مثلاً ، فهلك اثنان وبقي واحد، فله ذلك الباقي تمامه.
[3] قوله : فله ما بقي ; يعني الثلث الكامل منهما ، لكن هذا على تقدير أن يخرج هذا الباقي من ثلث ما بقي من جميع أصناف ماله ، كما صرح به في «الهداية». قال الفقيه أبو الليث الله : وقد اتفقوا على أنه لو استحق الدرهمان، وبقي الدرهم فالدرهم للموصى له، وكذلك إذا هلك الدرهمان، وبقى الدرهم. كذا في الجلبي»
[4] قوله : ويمكن جمع حق أحد المستحقين ; أي يمكن جمع حق شائع لكلِّ واحدٍ في فرد.
(1) المائدة : 48 .
(2) «ذخيرة العقبی» (ص619).
Section: And in 'in a sixth of my property' repeated, he gets a sixth, because when a definite noun is repeated as definite, the second is the same as the first. And with 'a third of his dirhams, or of his sheep, or of his clothes of different types, or of his slaves, if two-thirds of them perish, he gets what remains in the first two, and one-third of the remainder in the latter two'. This is our view, and according to Zufar, one-third of the remainder in all cases, because the legatee's right is a share in the whole; so if one-third of the property perishes, two-thirds of the legatee's right perish. For us: the legatee's right takes precedence over the heirs' right, so wherever compulsory division is applicable, and it is possible to concentrate the legatee's right in one item [it is done]. [1] His statement: 'the second is the same as the first' is the most common in language, but if evidence indicates that the second means something else, it is not the same, as in His statement: 'And We have sent down to you the Book in truth, confirming what was before it of the Scripture' (5:48). Thus in al-Kifayah. [2] His statement: 'if two-thirds perish' means two-thirds of the dirhams or sheep, for example if there were three, two perished and one remained, then he gets that remaining one entirely. [3] His statement: 'he gets what remains' means the complete third of them, but this is on condition that this remainder comes from the third of what remains of all types of his property, as stated in al-Hidayah. Abu al-Layth said: They agreed that if two dirhams are taken (by legatee? context may mean: if two dirhams were the legatee's share? Actually it says: if two dirhams are rightfully taken/claimed?) and one dirham remains, then that dirham is for the legatee; similarly if two dirhams perish and one remains. Thus in al-Jalabi. [4] His statement: 'It is possible to concentrate the right of one of the entitled parties' means that the common right of each can be concentrated in one individual. (1) Surah al-Ma'idah: 48. (2) Dhakhirat al-Uqba (p.619).
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings on wills. First: if the testator says 'in a sixth of my property' twice, the legatee gets one sixth because repeating a definite noun makes it the same (linguistic rule). Second: if the testator bequeaths 'a third of his dirhams, sheep, clothes (different types), or slaves' and then two-thirds of that property perishes, the Hanafi ruling differs by type: for dirhams and sheep (fungibles), the legatee takes the entire remaining one-third (i.e., the whole surviving property from that category); for clothes (diverse) and slaves (unique items), he takes only one-third of the remaining property. Zufar holds he takes one-third of the remaining in all cases. The Hanafi proof: the legatee's right is prior to the heirs', and since compulsory division (jabr) is possible, the legatee can take his entire share from the surviving property. The annotations explain the linguistic rule with a Qur'anic example, clarify the scenario of destruction, and confirm agreement on a specific case.

Key Terms
المعرفة (al-ma'rifah): A definite noun; repeating it as definite indicates the same referent.
الموصى له (al-musa lahu): The legatee, the person receiving the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Repeating a definite noun as definite in a bequest refers to the same share; only one share is executed unless evidence shows a different intention.

Bequest of a Third of Property When Part Perishes: Hanafi Ruling and Zufar's Dispute
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest of a third when part perishes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling for fungible vs non-fungible property in bequests when part perishes, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
For fungibles, legatee takes the whole surviving property; for non-fungibles, only one-third of the survivor.

This passage addresses a nuanced scenario: a testator bequeaths 'a third of his dirhams, sheep, diverse clothes, or slaves,' but two-thirds of that property perishes before the testator's death. The Hanafi school gives different results depending on whether the property is fungible (dirhams, sheep) or non-fungible (clothes, slaves). Zufar, a prominent Hanafi imam, disagrees and treats all cases uniformly. We will analyze the proofs and the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the property
Identify whether the bequeathed property is fungible (mithli: dirhams, sheep) or non-fungible (qimi: diverse clothes, slaves).
Fungibles are interchangeable; non-fungibles are unique.
2
Apply the destruction scenario
Assume two-thirds of the property perishes. For fungibles, the legatee takes the entire remaining third. For non-fungibles, he takes one-third of the remainder.
Example: 3 dirhams, 2 perish => legatee gets the 1 remaining dirham. 3 unique garments, 2 perish => legatee gets 1/3 of the remaining garment.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The legatee's right is prior to the heirs' right. Where compulsory division (jabr) is possible (with fungibles), the legatee can take his entire share from the surviving property. For non-fungibles, forced division is not possible, so he only gets a proportional share.
The key is the ability to concentrate the legatee's share without causing loss to heirs.
4
Note Zufar's opposition
Zufar holds that the legatee gets one-third of the remaining property in all cases, because his right is a share in the whole; destruction reduces proportionally.
Zufar sees no distinction based on property type.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa with Sahibayn) is relied upon, as stated in al-Hidayah: the distinction stands.
This is the view for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وفي سدس مالي مكرراً ، له سدس؛ لأنَّ المعرفة إذا أعيدت معرفة كان الثاني عين الأول.
وبثُلُثِ دراهمه ، أو غنمه ، أو ثيابه متفاوتة، أو عبيده إن هلك ثلثاه فله ما بقي في الأولين وثلث الباقي في الآخرين، هذا عندنا وعند زُفَرَه ثُلُثُ الباقي في كل الصور ; لأن حق الموصى له شائع في الجميع، فإذا هَلَكَ ثُلث المال هَلَكَ ثلثا حق الموصى له لنا : أنّ حق الموصى له مقدم على حق الورثة ، فكل ما يجري فيه الجبر على القسمة، ويمكنُ جَمْعُ حق أحد المستحقين في الواحد :
[1] قوله : كان الثاني عين الأوّل ; وهو الأعم الأغلب في اللغة، أما إذا دل الدليل على أنه أريد بالثاني غير الأول لم يكن عينه إذا كما في قوله : وَأَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الْكِتَبَ بِالْحَقِّ مُصَدِّقًا لِمَا بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ مِنَ الْكِتَب (1). كذا في «الكفاية».

The Repeated Sixth in Bequests
Linguistic rule in bequest interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that repeating a definite noun designates the same entity and apply it to determine that a second 'sixth' does not create an additional share.

Core Idea
Repeating 'a sixth of my wealth' means the same sixth, not an additional one.

In Arabic, when a definite noun (like 'al-sudus') is repeated in the same context, the second refers to the same entity. This linguistic rule has legal consequences in wills. This lesson examines its application when a testator says 'a sixth of my wealth' twice, and how Hanafi jurists determine that the legatee receives only one sixth total.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic principle
Note the rule: when a definite noun is repeated as definite, the second occurrence designates the same entity as the first. Example: 'al-kitab' repeated in Quran 5:48 refers to the same book.
This is the default rule unless context indicates otherwise.
2
Apply to the bequest scenario
The testator says 'a sixth of my wealth' twice (مكرراً). According to the rule, the second 'a sixth' is the same as the first, not an additional sixth.
Thus the legatee gets one sixth total, not two sixths.
3
Understand the exception
If there is evidence (dalil) that the testator intended a different sixth, the rule does not apply. The text cites that the principle is the dominant usage (الأعم الأغلب) but can be overridden.
No such evidence here, so the legatee receives only one sixth.
4
Confirm the legal outcome
The legatee's share is one sixth of the estate, not two sixths. This avoids ambiguity and protects the heirs from excessive claims.
This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi approach to clear expression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi commentary deals with two issues in bequests (wasaya). First, if someone bequeaths 'a sixth of my wealth' and then repeats 'a sixth of my wealth,' the second refers to the same sixth, not an additional sixth, because when a definite noun is repeated, it designates the same entity in Arabic. Second, the passage addresses bequests of a third of specific types of property (dirhams, sheep, diverse clothes, slaves). If two-thirds of the property is destroyed, the legatee takes what remains in the divisible types (dirhams and sheep) and one-third of what remains from the indivisible types (clothes and slaves). This is the Hanafi position. Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagrees, holding that the legatee only gets one-third of what remains in all cases because his right is undivided in the whole. The Hanafi proof is that the legatee's right is given priority over the heirs', so when property is destroyed, the loss is attributed to the heirs' portion first, not the legatee's. The commentary elaborates on the Arabic language rule with a Quranic example (5:48) and clarifies that the legatee gets the remaining item fully if only one remains from a divisible type, provided it comes from the one-third of what remains of all property.

Key Terms
معرفة (ma'rifah): A definite noun (e.g., 'al-sudus'). Repetition of a definite noun indicates identity.
المكرر (al-mukarrar): The repeated (word or phrase), here referring to the second occurrence of 'a sixth'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One sixth
B) Two sixths (one third)
C) The bequest is void due to ambiguity
D) It depends on the type of property

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, repeating a definite noun in a bequest does not create an additional share; the rule of identity applies unless evidence shows otherwise.

Legatee's Right When Bequest Property Is Destroyed: Hanafi vs Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that the legatee takes the remaining property when part is destroyed, distinguish between divisible and indivisible property, and contrast the Hanafi position with Zufar's proportional view.

Core Idea
The legatee's right has priority; destruction is attributed to heirs, not legatee.

When a testator bequeaths a third of specific property (like dirhams, sheep, clothes, or slaves) and part of that property is destroyed, how much does the legatee receive? The Hanafi school distinguishes between divisible and indivisible property: for divisible items, the legatee takes whatever remains fully; for indivisible items, he takes one-third of what remains. Zufar, an early Hanafi scholar, holds that in all cases the legatee gets one-third of the remainder. This lesson examines the reasoning behind both positions and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of property
The text mentions two categories: divisible (dirhams, sheep) and indivisible (diverse clothes, slaves). This distinction is crucial.
Divisible items can be split without loss of value; indivisible cannot.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each type
If two-thirds of divisible property (e.g., 3 dirhams, 2 destroyed) are destroyed, the legatee gets the remaining one dirham fully. If two-thirds of indivisible property (e.g., a set of clothes) are destroyed, the legatee gets one-third of what remains (e.g., one of the remaining garments).
The legatee's share is preserved as much as possible.
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The legatee's right is given priority over the heirs' right. Therefore, destruction is attributed to the heirs' portion, not the legatee's. In divisible property, the legatee can take the whole remaining item; in indivisible, only a share because the property cannot be divided.
The principle: حق الموصى له مقدم على حق الورثة.
4
Present Zufar's objection and his reasoning
Zufar says in all cases the legatee gets one-third of the remainder. His argument: the legatee's right is undivided (شائع) in the whole property. If one-third of the property is destroyed, two-thirds of the legatee's share (which was one-third of the whole) is also destroyed, leaving him with one-third of one-third = one-ninth of the original, which is one-third of the remaining one-third.
Zufar's view is a proportional allocation.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response: priority matters. The legatee's right is not proportional in the sense of sharing loss; rather, the loss falls on the heirs. This is supported by the practical possibility of giving the legatee the full remainder in divisible cases. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in divisible property, Hanafi gives full remainder; Zufar gives one-third of remainder.

Source Text

Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi commentary deals with two issues in bequests (wasaya). First, if someone bequeaths 'a sixth of my wealth' and then repeats 'a sixth of my wealth,' the second refers to the same sixth, not an additional sixth, because when a definite noun is repeated, it designates the same entity in Arabic. Second, the passage addresses bequests of a third of specific types of property (dirhams, sheep, diverse clothes, slaves). If two-thirds of the property is destroyed, the legatee takes what remains in the divisible types (dirhams and sheep) and one-third of what remains from the indivisible types (clothes and slaves). This is the Hanafi position. Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagrees, holding that the legatee only gets one-third of what remains in all cases because his right is undivided in the whole. The Hanafi proof is that the legatee's right is given priority over the heirs', so when property is destroyed, the loss is attributed to the heirs' portion first, not the legatee's. The commentary elaborates on the Arabic language rule with a Quranic example (5:48) and clarifies that the legatee gets the remaining item fully if only one remains from a divisible type, provided it comes from the one-third of what remains of all property.

Key Terms
الموصى له (al-mūṣā lahu): The person to whom a bequest is made; the legatee.
الورثة (al-warathah): The heirs who inherit by shares after debts and bequests.
شائع (shā'i'): Undivided share; a fractional interest in the whole property.
جبر على القسمة (jabr 'alā al-qismah): Mandatory division; the process by which co-owners are compelled to divide joint property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third of his three dirhams to Zayd, and two dirhams are destroyed, how much does Zayd receive according to the Hanafi school?
A) One dirham (the remaining one)
B) One-third of a dirham
C) Nothing, the bequest is void
D) Two-thirds of a dirham

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, destruction of bequeathed property is attributed to the heirs, not the legatee; the legatee's right is preserved as much as possible, taking the full remainder in divisible property and a proportionate share in indivisible.

Bequest from Mixed Cash and Debt
Ruling on bequest from mixed assets with proportional sharing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for allocating a bequest from an estate consisting of both cash and debt.

Core Idea
A bequest is paid from cash first; if insufficient, the legatee shares proportionally in cash and collected debt.

When a testator bequeaths a fixed amount, but the estate contains both cash and a debt owed to him, how should the legatee be paid? The Hanafi school protects the heirs by ensuring the legatee does not take only cash (which is preferred), but shares proportionally in both assets. This lesson unpacks the rule from al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and estate composition
The testator bequeaths 1,000 dirhams. His estate has cash (عين) and a debt (دين) due to him. Determine if the cash alone is sufficient to cover the bequest from one-third of the cash.
One-third of the cash is the maximum the legatee can take from cash, since the bequest is limited to one-third of the estate.
2
Check if bequest can be fully paid from cash
If the cash alone is at least 3,000 dirhams, then one-third of the cash (1,000) covers the bequest. In that case, the legatee receives the full amount from cash only.
This is because the bequest can be fulfilled without affecting the debt collection.
3
Apply proportional sharing when cash is insufficient
If the cash is less than 3,000 (e.g., 2,000), the legatee receives one-third of the cash (666.67) plus one-third of any debt collected later, until he reaches 1,000.
The legatee is a partner with the heirs; giving him only cash would harm the heirs, as cash is superior to debt (immediately available).
4
Ascertain the legal rationale (ta'lil)
The reasoning: the legatee is a partner (شريك) of the heir in the estate. Assigning him solely to cash (which has a superior quality) would be unfair to the heirs. Hence, he must share proportionally in both cash and debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبألف وله عين ودين، هو عين إن خَرَجَ من ثلث العين، وإلا ثلث العين، وثلث ما يؤخذ من الدين، وبثلث لزيد وعمرو، وعمرو ميت كله لزيد، فإن قال : بينهما، فنصفه له) : أي إن قال : ثلث مالي بين زيد وعمرو ، وهو ميت، فلزيد نصفُ الثَّلث ؛ لأنه صريح في أن لزيد نصف الثلث.
[1] قوله : وبألف وله... الخ ؛ حاصله ومن أوصى لرجل بألف درهم، وله مال عين ودين على الآخر، فإن خرج الألف من ثلث العين بأن كان له ثلاث آلاف درهم دفع إلى الموصى له ؛ لأنه أمكن إيفاء كل ذي حق حقه من غير نقصان. فيصار إليه وإلا أي وإن لم يخرج الألف من ثلث العين، بأن كان ألفا درهم نقداً، دفع إليه ثلث العين وثلث ما يؤخذ من الدين ؛ أي كل ما خرج شيء من الدين أخذ الموصى له ثلثه، حتى يستوفي الألف ؛ لأنَّ الموصى له شريك الوارث، وفي تخصيصه العين بخس في حق الورثة ؛ لأنّ للعين فضلاً على الدين. كذا في «الهداية»(۲). [٢] قوله : لأن الوصية عنده ؛ أي عند الموصي صحيحة، بناء على اعتقاده
And with one thousand and he has cash and debt: it is cash if it comes out of the third of the cash; otherwise, one-third of the cash and one-third of what is taken from the debt. And with a third to Zayd and 'Amr, and 'Amr is dead: it all goes to Zayd. If he says 'between them,' then half of it is his. That is, if he says 'a third of my wealth between Zayd and 'Amr' and 'Amr is dead, then Zayd gets half of the third, because it explicitly states that Zayd gets half of the third.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct bequest scenarios. First, a man bequeaths one thousand dirhams but his estate consists of both cash (عين) and a debt owed to him (دين). If the one thousand can be taken from one-third of the cash (i.e., his cash is three thousand or more), then the legatee gets the full amount from cash. Otherwise, he receives one-third of the cash and one-third of any debt collected, until he gets his thousand. The reason, as stated in al-Hidayah, is that the legatee is a partner with the heir, and assigning him solely to the cash would disadvantage the heirs, since cash is superior to debt. Second, a man bequeaths a third of his wealth to Zayd and 'Amr. If 'Amr is already dead at the time of the bequest, the entire third goes to Zayd if the testator did not know of 'Amr's death. The reasoning is that the testator's intention was to benefit a living person, and a dead person cannot be a legatee. However, if the testator said 'between them' explicitly, then Zayd gets only half of the third, because the wording is clear. A difference with Abu Yusuf is noted: if the testator was unaware of 'Amr's death, Abu Yusuf says Zayd gets only half, because the testator's belief that the bequest to 'Amr was valid means he only intended Zayd to have half.

Key Terms
عين (‘ayn): Tangible cash or property in hand, as opposed to debt receivable.
دين (dayn): A debt owed to the testator, which is part of the estate but not yet collected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths 800 dirhams. His estate has 1,000 dirhams cash and 3,000 dirhams debt. How much does the legatee receive from cash immediately?
A) 800 dirhams from cash.
B) 333.33 dirhams from cash (one-third of cash).
C) 500 dirhams from cash.
D) 400 dirhams from cash.

Key Takeaway
When an estate contains both cash and debt, a legatee must be paid proportionally from both, reflecting his role as a partner with the heirs.

Bequest of a Third to Two Persons When One Is Deceased
Ruling on bequest to two persons when one is deceased, with an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the share of the surviving legatee when a bequest of a third is made to two persons and one is deceased, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue.

Core Idea
If a legatee dies before the testator, his share goes to the other legatee, unless the testator explicitly divided it between them.

What happens when a testator bequeaths a third of his wealth to two people, but one of them is already dead at the time of the bequest? The Hanafi school holds that the surviving legatee takes the entire third, because a bequest to a dead person is void. However, Abu Yusuf differed if the testator was unaware of the death. This lesson examines the ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and the status of legatees
The testator says: 'a third of my wealth to Zayd and 'Amr'. Assume the testator is unaware that 'Amr is already dead. Determine if the bequest to 'Amr is valid.
A bequest to a deceased person is void because the legatee must be alive at the time of the testator's death.
2
Apply the general Hanafi rule
Since the bequest to 'Amr is void, the entire third goes to Zayd as the sole surviving legatee. The testator's ignorance does not affect the objective reality.
This is the majority position (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and later scholars).
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's exception
Abu Yusuf argues: if the testator believed 'Amr was alive, his intention was to give half the third to each. The surviving legatee should only get half, because the testator did not intend to give him the full third.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the tarjih (preferred view)
The majority view is relied upon (mufta bihi) because the bequest to a dead person is fundamentally invalid, and the testator's mistaken belief does not revive it. The surviving legatee takes all.
However, if the testator explicitly said 'between them' (بينهما), then Zayd receives only half of the third, as the wording is clear.

That is, if he says 'a third of my wealth between Zayd and 'Amr' and 'Amr is dead, then Zayd gets half of the third, because it explicitly states that Zayd gets half of the third.

If the one thousand can be taken from one-third of the cash (i.e., his cash is three thousand or more), then the legatee gets the full amount from cash. Bequest of a Fixed Amount with Mixed Assets and Predeceased Legatee
Ruling with proof on mixed asset bequest and predeceased legatee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of a bequest of a fixed amount when the estate includes both tangible assets and debts receivable, and apply the Hanafi rule that a bequest to a deceased person is void.

Core Idea
The legatee is a partner with the heir, so both tangible assets and debts must contribute proportionally.

This lesson examines two related rulings from the Hidayah on bequests (wasiyyah). First, how to fulfill a bequest of a specific sum when the testator leaves both cash (ayn) and debts owed to him (dayn) – a common scenario. Second, what happens when the testator bequeaths to two persons and one dies before him. These cases illustrate the Hanafi approach to balancing the rights of legatees and heirs while respecting the one-third limit.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Identify that the testator bequeaths a fixed amount (e.g., 1000 dirhams) and his estate consists of two types: tangible assets (ayn) and debts receivable (dayn). The bequest must be paid from the one-third of the total estate.
The legatee's share is limited to one-third of the entire estate, but the distribution between ayn and dayn is the issue.
2
Apply the primary rule for mixed assets
First, check if the bequest can be paid entirely from one-third of the tangible assets. If yes (e.g., tangible assets are at least 3000 dirhams), give the full bequest from tangible assets. If not, the legatee receives one-third of the tangible assets plus one-third of whatever is collected from the debt until the full bequest is satisfied.
The reasoning: the legatee and heir share the estate; giving solely from tangible assets would harm the heir because tangible assets are more readily available.
3
Analyze the case of a predeceased legatee
If the testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to Zayd and Amr, and Amr dies before the testator, the ruling depends on the testator's knowledge. If he knew, the entire one-third goes to Zayd. If he did not know, Abu Hanifa holds that Zayd gets all (since bequest to a dead person is void), while Abu Yusuf holds Zayd gets half, considering the testator's belief that the bequest was valid.
The key principle: 'the dead does not compete with the living' (al-mayyit la yuzahim al-hayy).
4
Differentiate the explicit wording
If the testator explicitly says 'one-third of my wealth is between Zayd and Amr', then Zayd gets half of that one-third regardless of knowledge, because the phrasing is clear in dividing the share.
The wording 'between them' (baynahuma) is a clear division, not a lump bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبألف وله عين ودين، هو عين إن خَرَجَ من ثلث العين، وإلا ثلث العين، وثلث ما يؤخذ من الدين، وبثلث لزيد وعمرو، وعمرو ميت كله لزيد، فإن قال : بينهما، فنصفه له
كالدراهم والغنم ، يجمعُ حق الموصى له فيه مقدَّماً)، فيجمعُ في الباقي بخلاف ما ليس كذلك : كالتياب المتفاوتة والعبيد.
وبألف وله) عين ودين، هو عين إن خَرَجَ مِن ثُلُثِ العين، وإلا ثلث العين، وثلث ما يؤخذ من الدين. وبثلث لزيد وعمرو، وعمرو ميت كله لزيد) ؛ لأنَّ الميت لا يزاحم الحي كما لو قال : لزيد وجدار ، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه إن لم يعلم بموته ، فله نصف الثلث ؛ لأنَّ الوصية عنده" صحيحة لعمرو ، فلم يرض للحي إلا بنصف الثلث بخلاف ما إذا عَلِمَ بموته ؛ لأنَّ الوصية للميت لغو، فيكون راضياً بتمام الثلث لزيد، فإن قال : بينهما، فنصفه له) : أي إن قال : ثلث مالي بين زيد وعمرو ، وهو ميت، فلزيد نصفُ الثَّلث ؛ لأنه صريح في أن لزيد نصف الثلث.
:

[٢] قوله : لأن الوصية عنده ؛ أي عند الموصي صحيحة، بناء على اعتقاده
And with a thousand and he has tangible property and debt, it is tangible property if it comes from one-third of the tangible property, otherwise one-third of the tangible property and one-third of what is taken from the debt. And with one-third for Zayd and Amr, and Amr is dead, all of it is for Zayd, for if he says: between them, then half of it is for him. Like dirhams and sheep, the right of the legatee is combined in it as a priority, so it is combined in the remainder, contrary to what is not like that: like varying clothes and slaves. And with a thousand and he has tangible property and debt, it is tangible property if it comes from one-third of the tangible property, otherwise one-third of the tangible property and one-third of what is taken from the debt. And with one-third for Zayd and Amr, and Amr is dead, all of it is for Zayd; because the dead does not compete with the living, as if he said: for Zayd and a wall. And from Abu Yusuf: if he did not know of his death, then he has half of the one-third; because according to him the bequest is valid for Amr, so he was not satisfied for the living except with half of the one-third, contrary to if he knew of his death; because the bequest for the dead is void, so he is satisfied with the entire one-third for Zayd. If he says: between them, then half of it is for him. That is, if he says: one-third of my wealth is between Zayd and Amr, and he is dead, then Zayd has half of the one-third; because it is explicit that Zayd has half of the one-third. ... Summary: And whoever bequeaths to a man a thousand dirhams, and he has wealth in tangible property and debt owed by another, if the thousand comes from one-third of the tangible property, e.g., he has three thousand dirhams, he gives it to the legatee; because it is possible to fulfill each right-holder's right without reduction. So one proceeds to that. Otherwise, i.e., if the thousand does not come from one-third of the tangible property, e.g., he has two thousand dirhams cash, he gives him one-third of the tangible property and one-third of what is taken from the debt; i.e., whenever something is collected from the debt, the legatee takes one-third of it, until he receives the thousand; because the legatee is a partner of the heir, and specifying the tangible property would be a loss to the heirs' right; because tangible property has preference over debt. As in al-Hidayah. [2] He said: because the bequest according to him; i.e., according to the testator, it is valid, based on his belief.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah on how to execute a bequest of a fixed amount (thousand dirhams) when the testator's estate consists of both tangible assets (ayn) and debts receivable (dayn). The ruling: first check if the thousand can be taken entirely from one-third of the tangible assets (i.e., total tangible assets are at least 3000 dirhams). If so, give the thousand entirely from the tangible assets. If not (e.g., tangible assets are only 2000 dirhams), then the legatee receives one-third of the tangible assets (666.66 dirhams) plus one-third of whatever is collected from the debt, until the full thousand is paid. The reasoning: the legatee shares with the heir; if we only gave from tangible assets, it would harm the heir because tangible assets are preferable (easier to realize) than debts. Hence both must contribute proportionally. The passage also discusses a subsidiary case: if the testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to Zayd and Amr, but Amr dies before the testator. The ruling: if the testator knew of Amr's death, the entire one-third goes to Zayd (since bequest to a dead person is void). If the testator did not know, then according to Abu Yusuf, the bequest to Amr is considered valid in the testator's intent, so Zayd only gets half of the one-third, and the other half remains with the heirs. The text also clarifies that if the testator explicitly says 'one-third between Zayd and Amr', then Zayd gets half of the one-third regardless of knowledge. The underlying principle: 'the dead does not compete with the living'.

Key Terms
عين (ayn): Tangible property physically present, such as cash, goods, real estate.
دين (dayn): Debt receivable, i.e., money owed to the testator by others.
وصية (wasiyyah): A testamentary bequest of property to another, taking effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths 1000 dirhams, and his estate consists of 2000 dirhams in cash (ayn) and 1000 dirhams owed to him (dayn), how much does the legatee receive from the cash?
A) 1000 dirhams from cash
B) One-third of the cash, i.e., 666.66 dirhams
C) None from cash, all from the debt
D) Half of the debt, i.e., 500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
A bequest of a fixed sum is fulfilled proportionally from tangible assets and debts, and a bequest to a deceased person is void, giving the entire share to the surviving legatee.

Bequest of One-Third When Testator Is Poor
Ruling on bequest validity when testator has no property at time of will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the validity of a bequest depends on the existence of the bequeathed property at death, and distinguish between bequests expressed as a fraction versus a specific item.

Core Idea
A bequest is judged at death: property acquired after the will counts if the wording is general.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: a testator makes a bequest while poor, then later acquires wealth. The Hanafi school holds that the bequest is valid if the property exists at death. However, the wording matters: a general bequest of 'one-third of my wealth' includes after-acquired property, while a bequest of a specific item from a flock that does not exist becomes void. Let's examine the three rulings and their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three distinct bequest scenarios: (1) bequest of one-third of wealth when poor, (2) bequest of one-third of sheep when no sheep, (3) bequest of a sheep from wealth vs from flock. Note the different outcomes.
2
Understand the key condition
The fundamental principle is that a bequest is a contract that takes effect after death. Therefore, the existence of the bequeathed property at the time of death is what matters, not at the time of the will.
3
Analyze the wording
The wording determines whether the bequest is for a monetary value or a specific item. 'From my wealth' indicates value; 'from my flock' indicates a specific physical item.
4
Note the correct view on later acquisition
If the testator later acquires the type of property (e.g., sheep), the bequest of 'one-third of my sheep' becomes valid according to the correct view (al-sahih). This is because existence at death is what counts.
5
Apply the principle to similar cases
Practice applying this rule to other scenarios, such as bequests of shares, livestock, or specific heirlooms, to internalize the condition.

[۲]
C
(وبشاة من مالي ، أو غنمي، ولا شاءَ له قيمتها في مالي، وبطلت في غنمي)، فإنَّه إذا قال: له شاءٌ من مالي ولا شاة له، عُلِمَ أَنَّ المراد ماليةُ الشَّاة، وإذا قال : له شاة من غنمي، ولا غنم له ، يراد به عين الشاة، وليست موجودة، فتبطل الوصية. لحياته ، فلم يرضَ فذلك الموصي لزيد إلا بنصف الثلث، فيعطي له ذلك، فبقي النصفُ الآخر منه في أيدي ورثة الموصى.
[ ١ ] قوله : عند موته ؛ لأنّ الوصيّة عقد استحلاف مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت ، ويثبت حكمها بعد الموت، فيشترط وجود المال عند الموت لا قبله.
[٢] قوله: تصح؛ لأنها لو كانت بلفظ المال تصح كما مر آنفاً ، فكذا تصح إذا كانت باسم نوعه، وهذا لأنَّ وجود ما أوصى به قبل الموت فضل، والمعتبر قيامه عند الموت. كذا في «الهداية»).
And with one-third, and he is poor, he has one-third of his wealth at the time of his death. And with one-third of his sheep, and he has no sheep, or they perish before his death, it becomes void. And with a sheep from my wealth, or my flock, and he has no sheep, its value is in my wealth, and it becomes void in my flock. (And with one-third, and he is poor, he has one-third of his wealth at the time of his death): i.e., he said: one-third of my wealth, and the testator has no wealth, then he acquires wealth, so the legatee has one-third of the testator's wealth at the time of his death. (And with one-third of his sheep, and he has no sheep, or they perish before his death, it becomes void): His saying: 'and he has no sheep' means that he has no sheep at the time of the will, and he does not acquire sheep, until if he acquires sheep, then the correct view is that the bequest is valid. (And with a sheep from my wealth, or my flock, and he has no sheep, its value is in my wealth, and it becomes void in my flock): For if he says: he has a sheep from my wealth and he has no sheep, it is known that what is intended is the monetary value of the sheep. And if he says: he has a sheep from my flock, and he has no flock, what is intended is the actual sheep, and it is not present, so the bequest becomes void. [1] His saying: at the time of his death; because the bequest is a contract of obligation added to after death, and its ruling is established after death, so the existence of wealth is required at the time of death, not before. [2] His saying: it is valid; because if it was with the wording of wealth, it is valid as previously mentioned, so also it is valid if it is by the name of its type. And this is because the existence of what is bequeathed before death is a surplus, and what is considered is its existence at the time of death. As in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage contains three distinct rulings from the Hidayah. First ruling: If a person says 'I bequeath one-third of my wealth' but at the time of the will he is poor (no wealth), and later acquires wealth before death, the bequest is valid and the legatee gets one-third of the wealth as it exists at the time of death. Reason: the bequest is a contract that takes effect after death; the existence of the bequeathed property at the time of death is what matters, not at the time of the will. Second ruling: If a person bequeaths 'one-third of my sheep' but has no sheep at the time of the will and never acquires any, or the sheep perish before the testator's death, the bequest becomes void. However, if the testator later acquires sheep, the bequest is valid (according to the correct view). Third ruling: If a person bequeaths 'a sheep from my wealth' and has no sheep, the bequest is valid and the legatee receives the value of a sheep from the general wealth; because 'from my wealth' indicates that the monetary value is intended. But if he bequeaths 'a sheep from my flock' and has no flock, the bequest is void because the specific item (a sheep from a flock) is intended and cannot be found.

Key Terms
فقير (faqir): A person who has no property at the time of making the will.
بطلت (batulat): The bequest becomes void, i.e., ineffective, because the subject matter does not exist at death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 1000 dirhams
C) 3000 dirhams
D) It depends on the heirs' consent

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bequest hinges on the existence of the property at death, not at the time of the will, unless the wording specifies a particular existing item.

Bequest of a Sheep from Wealth vs. Flock
Distinction between bequest of a sheep from general wealth and from a specific flock

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a bequest of a sheep 'from my wealth' and 'from my flock' and state the ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
Wording matters: 'from my wealth' implies value; 'from my flock' implies a specific animal.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a subtle but important distinction in bequests. The key is the prepositional phrase: whether the testator says 'from my wealth' or 'from my flock'. This seemingly small difference determines whether the bequest is executed by paying the value or becomes void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases
Carefully read the bequest wording: 'min mali' (from my wealth) vs 'min ghanami' (from my flock).
The particle 'min' is critical.
2
Determine the testator's situation
In both cases the testator has no sheep. The ruling hinges on the interpretation of the phrase.
3
Apply the rule of interpretation
For 'min mali', the word 'mal' (wealth) is general and includes monetary value, so the bequest is construed as a gift of value. For 'min ghanami', 'ghanam' (flock) refers to specific animals, so the bequest requires an actual sheep.
Hanafi principles of interpretation: al-haqiqah al-shar'iyyah vs al-haqiqah al-urfiyyah.
4
Derive the ruling
From 'min mali': the legatee receives the value of a sheep from the estate – the bequest is valid. From 'min ghanami': the bequest is void because the subject does not exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وبشاة من مالي ، أو غنمي، ولا شاءَ له قيمتها في مالي، وبطلت في غنمي)، فإنَّه إذا قال: له شاءٌ من مالي ولا شاة له، عُلِمَ أَنَّ المراد ماليةُ الشَّاة، وإذا قال : له شاة من غنمي، ولا غنم له ، يراد به عين الشاة، وليست موجودة، فتبطل الوصية.
(And with a sheep from my wealth, or my flock, and he has no sheep, its value is in my wealth, and it becomes void in my flock): For if he says: he has a sheep from my wealth and he has no sheep, it is known that what is intended is the monetary value of the sheep. And if he says: he has a sheep from my flock, and he has no flock, what is intended is the actual sheep, and it is not present, so the bequest becomes void.
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage parses the distinction between a bequest of a sheep 'from my wealth' (min mali) versus 'from my flock' (min ghanami). In the first case, since the testator has no specific sheep, the phrase 'from my wealth' indicates that the legatee is to receive the value (price) of a sheep from the general estate. The bequest is valid and the heir must give the value. In the second case, the phrase 'from my flock' implies an actual sheep belonging to a specific flock. Since there is no flock, the bequest has no subject matter and becomes void. The key is the wording: 'wealth' is general and includes values; 'flock' is specific to actual animals.

Key Terms
مال (mal): General wealth or property, which includes monetary value.
غنم (ghanam): A specific flock of sheep or goats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The bequest is void
B) The legatee receives a sheep from the heirs' property
C) The legatee receives the value of a sheep from the estate
D) The bequest is postponed until the testator acquires a sheep

Key Takeaway
The wording of a bequest determines whether it is fulfilled by value or becomes void if the specific item is absent.

Bequest of a Third When Testator Has No Property
Ruling on bequest of a third of property and flock when property is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a bequest when the bequeathed property does not exist at the time of the will, and explain why existence at death is the decisive condition.

Core Idea
A bequest is valid even if the property is nonexistent at the time of the will, as long as it exists at death.

This lesson clarifies a common point of confusion in Hanafi wasiyyah law: what if a testator bequeaths a third of his sheep, but owns no sheep at the time of the will? Does the bequest become void? The text teaches us that the critical moment is the testator's death, not the making of the will. Understanding this distinction is essential for drafting valid bequests and avoiding disputes between heirs and legatees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The text presents a testator who is poor (faqir) and bequeaths a third of his property or a third of his flock, but he owns no such property at the time of the will.
Note the two separate cases: bequest of 'a third of his wealth' and 'a third of his flock'.
2
Recognize the potential invalidity
If the bequeathed item does not exist at any time, the bequest is void. However, the question is whether the lack of existence at the time of the will is fatal.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
The text states that the will is a contract of obligation deferred to after death (عقد استحلاف مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت). Therefore, the condition of existence is connected to the time of death, not the time of the will.
This principle derives from the nature of wasiyyah as a transaction that takes effect only after death (tabi'at al-mawt).
4
Derive the ruling for the scenario
If the testator acquires the flock before death, the bequest is valid. If he never acquires it, or if it perishes before death, the bequest becomes void.
This distinction applies equally to bequests of a generic category (thuluth al-ghana'm) and to bequests expressed in terms of 'wealth' (mal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلث، وهو فقير، له ثلث ماله عند موته، وبثُلُثِ غَنَمِه، ولا غَنَمَ له، أو هَلَكَ قبل موته ، بطلت، [١] قوله : عند موته ; لأنّ الوصيّة عقد استحلاف مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت، ويثبت حكمها بعد الموت، فيشترط وجود المال عند الموت لا قبله. [٢] قوله: ولا غنم له، معناه: أنه لا غنم له عند الوصية، ولم يستفد غنماً، حَتَّى إِن استفادَ غَنَمَا، فالصحيح أن الوصية تصح; لأنها لو كانت بلفظ المال تصح كما مر آنفاً، فكذا تصح إذا كانت باسم نوعه، وهذا لأنَّ وجود ما أوصى به قبل الموت فضل، والمعتبر قيامه عند الموت. كذا في «الهداية»).
And with a third, while he is poor, he has a third of his wealth at his death; and with a third of his flock, while he has no flock, or it perishes before his death, it becomes void. [1] His statement: 'at his death' because the will is a contract of obligation deferred to after death, and its ruling is established after death, so the existence of wealth at death is required, not before. [2] His statement: 'and he has no flock' means he has no flock at the time of the will, and he did not acquire a flock, until if he does acquire a flock, then the correct view is that the will is valid; because if it were in terms of wealth it would be valid as mentioned previously, so likewise it is valid when expressed by its type name, and this is because the existence of what was bequeathed before death is superfluous, and what is considered is its presence at death. Thus it is in Al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on bequests (wasiyyah) where the testator is poor and bequeaths a third of his property or a third of his flock when he does not currently own it. The commentary explains that the validity of the bequest depends on the existence of the bequeathed item at the time of the testator's death, not at the time the will is made. Therefore, if the testator acquires wealth or sheep before death, the bequest is effective. The reasoning is that a will is a deferred contract, so the condition of existence applies at death. The authority is Al-Hidayah, which represents the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will, a contract deferring transfer of ownership to after death.
ثلث (thuluth): One third of the estate, the maximum Quranic share that can be bequeathed to non-heirs.
غنم (ghanam): Sheep and goats collectively; a type of livestock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) At the time of the testator's death
C) At the time of acceptance by the legatee
D) At the time of the testator's birth

Key Takeaway
A bequest is valid even if the bequeathed property does not exist at the time of the will, as long as it exists at the testator's death.

Bequest of a Sheep: Phrasing Matters
Ruling on bequest phrasing when item absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequeathing a non-existent item and apply the distinction between 'from my wealth' and 'from my flock' phrasing.

Core Idea
Bequeathing a non-existent item is valid if phrased as value from wealth, invalid if tied to a specific flock.

A testator may wish to bequeath a sheep but own no sheep at death. Does the bequest fail entirely? This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle: the phrasing of the bequest determines whether the value can be given or the bequest is void. The passage from Al-Hidayah also refines the ruling by comparing two classical wordings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and its phrasing
Read the exact wording of the bequest. Does it say 'from my wealth' or 'from my flock'? This determines the legal analysis.
2
Determine if the specific item exists
The testator has no sheep. Confirm that the physical item is absent at the time of death.
If the item exists, the bequest is valid regardless of phrasing.
3
Apply the rule of idafah (attribution)
If the bequest is attributed to 'my wealth', the intention is the monetary value (maliyyah), which exists in the estate. If attributed to 'my flock', the intention is a specific physical sheep, which does not exist.
Hanafi usul: idafah clarifies the subject matter.
4
Conclude validity or invalidity
If 'from my wealth': valid → give value of a sheep. If 'from my flock' (and no flock): invalid (batil).
The same applies if the testator says only 'a sheep' without idafah – invalid per the stronger view.
5
Note the textual precision of Al-Hidayah vs Al-Matn
Al-Hidayah says 'no flock' (ghanaam), covering both no sheep at all and having one sheep but no flock. Al-Matn says 'no sheep' (shah), only covering the first case. Both lead to invalidity under 'from my flock' scenario, but Hidayah is more comprehensive.
This shows meticulous Hanafi concern for wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبشاةٍ من مالي، أو غنمي ولا شاة له قيمتها في مالي، وبطلت في غنمي [٣] قوله : من مالي ; ولا شاة له، وليس له شاة يعطي قيمة شاة ; لأنه لما أضاف إلى المالِ علم أنّ مراده الوصيّة بماليّة الشاة، إذ ماليتها توجد في مطلق المال، ومالية الشاة هي القيمة. أما إذا أوصى بشاة ولم يضفه إلى ماله وليس له شاة، قيل : لا يصح; لأنَّ المصحح هو الإضافة إلى المال، وبدونها تعتبر صورة الشاة ومعناها. (1) (الهداية). واعلم أنه قال في «الهداية» : ولا غَنَمَ له. وقال في «المتن»: ولا شاة له. وبينهما فرق ; لأنَّ الشاة فردّ من الغَنَم، فإذا لم يكن له شاة لا يكون له غنم، لكن إذا لم يكن له غنم لا يلزم أن لا يكون له شاة ; لاحتمال أن يكون له واحد لا كثير، فعبارة «الهداية» تناولت صورتين ما إذا لم يكن له شاة أصلاً، وما يكون له شاة، لكن لا غنم له، ففي الصورتين تبطل الوصية، وعبارة «المتن» لم تتناول إلاّ الصورة الأولى، ولم يعلم منها الحكم في الصورة الثانية، فعبارة «الهداية» أشمل، لكن هذه أحوط. هذا ما يستفاد من «الهداية»(۲).
And with a sheep from my wealth, or from my flock, and he has no sheep: its value is in my wealth, and it becomes void in my flock. [3] His statement: 'from my wealth' and he has no sheep, and he does not have a sheep, he is given the value of a sheep; because when he added it to wealth, it is known that his intent is the bequest of the monetary value of the sheep, since its monetary value exists in absolute wealth, and the monetary value of the sheep is its price. As for if he bequeaths a sheep without adding it to his wealth and he does not have a sheep, it is said: it is not valid; because the validating factor is the addition to wealth, and without it, the form and meaning of the sheep are considered. (1) Al-Hidayah. And know that he said in Al-Hidayah: 'and no flock for him.' And he said in Al-Matn: 'and no sheep for him.' And there is a difference between them; because the sheep is an individual of the flock, so if he does not have a sheep, he has no flock, but if he does not have a flock, it does not necessarily mean he has no sheep; because it is possible that he has one and not many. So the wording of Al-Hidayah covers two cases: where he has no sheep at all, and where he has a sheep but no flock. In both cases, the bequest becomes void. The wording of Al-Matn only covers the first case, and the ruling for the second case is not known from it. So the wording of Al-Hidayah is more comprehensive, but this is more precautionary. This is what is derived from Al-Hidayah (2).
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage addresses bequests of a specific item (a sheep) when the testator does not own it. The key distinction is the phrasing: if the testator says 'a sheep from my wealth', the bequest is interpreted as the value of a sheep, which is valid even if no sheep exists, because the value can be taken from the general wealth. However, if he says 'a sheep from my flock' and he has no flock, the bequest is invalid because it refers to a specific physical sheep, which does not exist. The commentary also compares the expressions in Al-Hidayah ('no flock') and Al-Matn ('no sheep'), noting that Al-Hidayah's wording covers more cases (both no sheep at all, and having a sheep but no flock), while Al-Matn only covers the first. The precautionary view follows Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
مالية (maliyyah): Monetary value or price of an item.
شاة (shah): A single sheep or goat.
إضافة (idafah): Attribution or addition; in this context, linking the bequest to 'my wealth' or 'my flock'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The bequest is valid and the heir gets the value
C) The bequest is invalid
D) The bequest is valid only if he acquires a flock before death

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on bequests of non-existent items hinges on phrasing: 'from my wealth' gives value; 'from my flock' invalidates.

Bequest to Ummahat Awlad: Division Dispute
Ruling on bequest of one third to ummahat awlad and poor, with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on dividing a bequest among ummahat awlad and the poor/needy, and explain why the bequest is valid by istihsan.

Core Idea
A bequest to ummahat awlad is valid by istihsan, but its division differs among the Hanafi masters.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on how to distribute a bequest of one third of the estate when the testator names three ummahat awlad (mothers of his children) and the poor and needy as beneficiaries. While all agree on the validity of such a bequest by istihsan, the division method differs between the two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute reveals the nuanced application of juristic preference and the practical impact of scholarly differences within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the bequest
The testator bequeaths one third of his estate to three ummahat awlad, the poor, and the needy. Note that the poor and needy are two distinct categories.
Ummahat awlad are slave women who bore children to the testator; they become free upon his death.
2
State the division of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the third is divided into five equal shares: each of the three women gets one fifth, the poor get one fifth, and the needy get one fifth.
Total of three fifths for the women, each one fifth.
3
State the division of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad divides the third into seven shares: the three women get three shares, the poor get two shares, and the needy get two shares.
This gives women a slightly smaller share per person (1/7 of third) compared to 1/5 in the other view.
4
Understand the basis of validity (istihsan)
The bequest to ummahat awlad is valid by istihsan because the testator's intention is that the bequest takes effect after their manumission, making it a valid will. Without istihsan, the bequest would be void since the women become free and inherit.
Istihsan allows departure from strict analogy to fulfill the testator's presumed intent.
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, each woman gets 1/15 of the total estate (1/5 of the third), while under Muhammad each woman gets 1/21. The poor and needy get more under Muhammad's division (2/21 each vs 1/15 each).
This difference matters in actual inheritance calculations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلث ماله لأمهات أولاده، وهنّ ثلاث، وللفقراء والمساكين لهن ثلاثة أخماس، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وعند محمد يقسم الثلث على سبعة أسهم، فلأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة منها ; لأن المذكور في الفقراء والمساكين [١] قوله : لهن ; أي لأمهات أولاده، وهن ثلث ثلاثة أخماس، فلكل واحد خمس وللفقراء خمس وللمساكين خمس. [٢] قوله : وعند محمد ... الخ ; توضيحه : إنّ الثلث يقسم على سبعة أسهم، لهنَّ ثلاثة أسهم، ولكل فريق من الفقراء والمساكين سهمان. وأصله : أنّ الوصية لأمَّهاتِ الأولادِ جائزة استحساناً ; لأنَّ الوصية مضافة إلى ما بعد عتقها لا حال حلول العتق بها بدلالة حال الموصي ; لأنَّ الظاهر من حال الموصي أنه يقصد بالإيصاء وصيّة صحيحة لا باطلة والوصية إنّما تصح إن لو كانت مضافةً إلى ما بعد عتقها، والفقراء والمساكين جنسان كما فسرنا في «كتاب الزكاة». (۱) انتهى من «الهداية»(٤ : ٢٣٩). (۲) «الهداية (٤) : ٢٣٩).
And with a third of his wealth for the mothers of his children, and they are three, and for the poor and the needy, for them three fifths. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, he divides the third into seven shares: for the mothers of his children three of them; because what is mentioned of the poor and needy... [1] His statement: 'for them' i.e. for the mothers of his children, and they are a third of three fifths, so each gets one fifth, and for the poor one fifth, and for the needy one fifth. [2] His statement: 'And according to Muhammad...' etc.; its clarification: The third is divided into seven shares: for them three shares, and for each group of the poor and needy two shares. The origin is that a bequest to the mothers of children is valid by istihsan; because the bequest is attached to after their manumission, not at the time of manumission, by the indication of the testator's state; because the apparent state of the testator is that he intends by his bequest a valid will, not an invalid one, and the will is only valid if it is attached to after their manumission. And the poor and needy are two categories as we explained in the Book of Zakat. (1) End from Al-Hidayah (4:239). (2) Al-Hidayah (4:239).
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of a bequest of one third of the estate to three ummahat awlad (mothers of the testator's children) and to the poor and needy (two categories). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the third is divided into five equal shares: each of the three ummahat awlad gets one fifth, the poor get one fifth, and the needy get one fifth (total three fifths for the three women? Actually the text says 'for them three fifths' meaning the three women collectively get three fifths, each one fifth). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the third is divided into seven shares: the three women get three shares (one share each), the poor get two shares, and the needy get two shares. The basis for the validity of the bequest to ummahat awlad is istihsan, because the intention is to make the bequest effective after their manumission (since umm walad becomes free upon the testator's death). The poor and needy are two distinct groups, as established in the Zakat chapter.

Key Terms
أمهات أولاد (ummahat awlad): Mothers of children (singular: umm walad) - slave women who bore a child to their master and consequently become free upon his death.
ثلث (thuluth): One third of the estate, the limit for bequests without heirs' consent.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning in Hanafi fiqh that allows departing from strict analogy for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, how many shares does the bequest of one third to three ummahat awlad and the poor and needy produce?
A) 5 shares
B) 7 shares
C) 3 shares
D) 9 shares

Key Takeaway
A bequest to ummahat awlad is valid by istihsan, but its division among them and other beneficiaries is subject to scholarly difference within the Hanafi school.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Distinguishing 'No Flock' from 'No Sheep' in Bequests
Linguistic-legal analysis of two will phrasings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal consequences of the expressions 'لا غنم له' and 'لا شاة له' in a will and apply the Hanafi ruling that invalidates the bequest in both scenarios covered by the more comprehensive phrasing.

Core Idea
A single sheep does not make a flock; the testator's wording determines the validity conditions.

In the Hanafi school, the precise wording of a bequest can determine whether it is valid or invalid. This lesson examines a subtle but important distinction between two similar phrases: 'لا غنم له' (he has no flock) and 'لا شاة له' (he has no sheep). The difference lies in the scope of coverage, and understanding it helps clarify the conditions under which a bequest of a sheep is enforceable. We will explore the reasoning from Al-Hidayah and Al-Matn, and see why the more comprehensive expression is considered more cautious (أحوط).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Expressions
Note the two phrases: 'لا غنم له' (no flock) and 'لا شاة له' (no sheep). Recognize that 'شاة' is a specific individual of the genus 'غنم'.
'غنم' is a collective noun, often understood as the genus.
2
Analyze the Logical Relationship
If a testator has no ewe, he certainly has no flock. But having no flock does not imply having no ewe; he may own a single ewe without a flock.
This is a linguistic inference based on part-whole relationship.
3
Determine Coverage of Each Expression
'لا غنم له' covers two scenarios: (a) no ewe at all, and (b) having a ewe but no flock. 'لا شاة له' covers only scenario (a).
4
Apply the Ruling
In both scenarios of 'لا غنم له', the bequest of a sheep is invalid (batil) because the specified object does not exist in the testator's ownership in the required form.
The condition for validity is that the bequeathed item must exist and be owned.
5
Compare the Two Rulings
Al-Hidayah's expression is more comprehensive (أشمل) and covers both problematic cases. Al-Matn's expression is less comprehensive but considered more cautious (أحوط) because it avoids the ambiguous second scenario by using a more specific term.
The more cautious approach prefers wording that leaves no room for doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه قال في «الهداية»: ولا غنم له. وقال في «المتن»: ولا شاة له. وبينهما فرق؛ لأن الشاة فرد من الغنم، فإذا لم يكن له شاة لا يكون له غنم، لكن إذا لم يكن له غنم لا يلزم أن لا يكون له شاة؛ لاحتمال أن يكون له واحد لا كثير، فعبارة «الهداية» تناولت صورتين: ما إذا لم يكن له شاة أصلاً، وما يكون له شاة لكن لا غنم له، ففي الصورتين تبطل الوصية، وعبارة «المتن» لم تتناول إلا الصورة الأولى، ولم يعلم منها الحكم في الصورة الثانية، فعبارة «الهداية» أشمل، لكن هذه أحوط.
Know that he said in Al-Hidayah: 'And he has no flock.' And he said in Al-Matn: 'And he has no ewe.' And between them is a difference; because the ewe is an individual of the flock, so if he does not have a ewe, he does not have a flock. But if he does not have a flock, it does not necessarily mean he does not have a ewe, because it is possible he has one but not many. So the expression of Al-Hidayah covers two scenarios: when he has no ewe at all, and when he has a ewe but no flock. In both scenarios the bequest is invalid. But the expression of Al-Matn only covers the first scenario, and the ruling in the second scenario is not known from it. So the expression of Al-Hidayah is more comprehensive, but this is more cautious.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage is a legal commentary explaining the distinction between two similar phrasings in the context of a bequest (وصية). The author compares the wording in Al-Hidayah ('لا غنم له' – he has no flock) and Al-Matn ('لا شاة له' – he has no ewe). The key difference is linguistic: 'شاة' (ewe) is a specific individual of the category 'غنم' (flock/generic sheep). If someone bequeaths 'a sheep from my flock' but owns no ewe, he certainly owns no flock. But if he owns no flock, he might still own a single ewe. Al-Hidayah's phrase covers both possibilities: total absence of sheep or presence of a ewe without a flock. In both, the bequest is invalid because the testator's intention to give a specific sheep cannot be fulfilled. Al-Matn's phrase only covers the first scenario, leaving uncertainty about the second. Thus Al-Hidayah's ruling is more comprehensive, but the author notes that Al-Matn's approach is more cautious (احوط). This analysis is based purely on linguistic inference and the testator's presumed intent.

Key Terms
الغنم (al-ghanam): A collective noun meaning flock of sheep or goats, used generically.
الشاة (al-shaah): A specific individual ewe or goat.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will, a legal device for transferring property after death.
أحوط (ahwat): More cautious; a term used when a ruling is prudent or preferred to avoid doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between 'لا غنم له' and 'لا شاة له' in terms of the scenarios they cover?
A) Both cover the same scenarios.
B) 'لا غنم له' covers two scenarios, 'لا شاة له' covers only one.
C) 'لا شاة له' is more comprehensive.
D) Neither covers the scenario of having a ewe but no flock.

Key Takeaway
The precise wording of a bequest determines its validity: 'لا غنم له' is more comprehensive, invalidating the will in two scenarios, while 'لا شاة له' covers only one scenario, making it more cautious.

Interpretation of Plural in Bequests: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on plural interpretation in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions in the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of the plural definite article (الجمع المحلى باللام) in bequests and apply each interpretation to calculate shares.

Core Idea
The plural with 'al-' can indicate the genus, not just numbers—thus one poor suffices for the plural in a bequest.

When a testator leaves one-third to 'the poor and needy,' does that mean one person or many? This lesson examines the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side, and Imam Muhammad on the other, over the interpretation of plural forms. The answer changes the share distribution significantly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Contested Phrase
The testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to specific beneficiaries. Key phrase: 'للفقراء والمساكين' (to the poor and needy). How should this plural be interpreted?
The plural is definite with 'al-'.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two) hold that the plural indicates the genus, so one individual from each group is enough. Imam Muhammad holds that the plural requires a minimum of two, by analogy to inheritance.
Imam Muhammad's view is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Examine the Proofs
The two cite Quran (33:52) 'لا يحل لك النساء' where 'النساء' is plural but refers to genus. Muhammad cites the hadith-like maxim 'الوصية أخت الميراث' and the rule that plural in inheritance requires two.
The proof is linguistic vs. analogical.
4
Apply to the Three Examples
First example: three mothers + poor + needy → two: 5 shares (3+1+1); Muhammad: 7 shares (3+2+2). Second example: one person + poor → two: half each; Muhammad: thirds (1+2). Third example: Zaid, Amr, partner → shares differ based on interpretation.
The practical difference is the number of shares.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text states that the understanding from the Sharh and glosses of Al-Hidayah supports the two's view, indicating it is the relied-upon position.
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلث ماله لأمهات أولاده، وهنّ ثلاث، وللفقراء والمساكين لهن ثلاثة أخماس، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وعند محمد يقسم الثلث على سبعة أسهم، فلأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة منها. لفظ الجمع، وأقله في الميراث اثنان، والوصية أخت الميراث. لهما: أن الجمع المحلى باللام يراد به الجنس، وتبطل الجمعية: كقوله: لا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ، فيراد به الواحد، فيقسم على خمسة، ولهنَّ ثلاثة منها. وبثلث له، وللفقراء نصف، له ونصف لهم، هذا عندهما، وعند محمد يقسم الثلث أثلاثاً. وبمئة لزيد، ومئة لعمرو، أو بها لزيد وخمسين لعمرو إن أشرك آخر معهما، فله ثلث ما لكلِّ في الأول، ونصفه في الثاني؛ لأن في الصورة الأولى لمحمد: إن المذكور في الفقراء والمساكين لفظ الجمع، وأقله في الميراث اثنان، نجد ذلك في القرآن، والوصية أخت الميراث كما مر، فكان لكل فريق من الفقراء والمساكين اثنان، وأمهات الأولاد ثلث، فباعتبار عدد الرؤوس يقسم الثلث على سبعة أسهم. ولهما: إن الجمع المحلى باللام يراد به الجنس وتبطل الجمعية؛ كقوله الله: لا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ، فيراد به الواحد والجنس، يتناول الأدنى مع احتمال الكل، لا سيما عند تعذر صرفه إلى الكل، فيعتبر من كل فريق واحد، فبلغ الحساب خمسة، فالثلاث للثلاث، والاثنان للاثنين. هكذا يفهم من عبارة الشرح وبعض حواشي الهداية. قوله: وإن أشرك آخر معهما؛ بأن قال لآخر: أشركتك معهما في الصورتين، فله ثلث الكل، واحد في الأول ونصفه في الثاني؛ لأن الشركة تقتضي المساواة.
And one-third of his wealth for the mothers of his children, and they are three, and for the poor and the needy, for them three-fifths. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, the third is divided into seven shares, so for the mothers of children three of them. The expression is plural, and its minimum in inheritance is two, and the will is akin to inheritance. For the two: that the plural with the definite article refers to the genus, and the plurality is negated: like His saying: 'Women are not permissible for you,' so it refers to the single, so it is divided into five, and for them three of them. And (the case of) one-third for him and half for the poor, for him half and half for them, this is according to the two, and according to Muhammad, the third is divided into three parts. And (the case of) one hundred for Zaid and one hundred for Amr, or one hundred for Zaid and fifty for Amr, if he includes another with them, then he gets one-third of what each gets in the first, and half in the second; because in the first scenario according to Muhammad: That which is mentioned for the poor and needy is a plural expression, and its minimum in inheritance is two, we find that in the Quran, and the will is akin to inheritance as stated, so for each group of the poor and needy there are two, and the mothers of children one-third, so according to the number of heads the third is divided into seven shares. And for the two: that the plural with the definite article refers to the genus and the plurality is negated; like Allah's saying: 'Women are not permissible for you,' so it refers to the single and the genus, encompassing the minimum with possibility of all, especially when it is impossible to refer to all, so from each group one is considered, so the calculation reaches five, so three for the three and two for the two. This is understood from the expression of the Sharh and some glosses of Al-Hidayah. His saying: And if he includes another with them; that is, he said to another: I include you with them in the two scenarios, then he gets one-third of the whole, one in the first and half in the second; because partnership demands equality.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of collective nouns (الجمع المحلى باللام) in bequests. The scenario: a testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth to three specific mothers of his children and to the poor and needy. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two) rule that the third is divided into five shares: three for the mothers, one for the poor, and one for the needy, because they interpret the plural 'the poor and needy' as referring to the genus, not a specific number. They cite the Quranic verse 'لا يحل لك النساء' where 'النساء' is a plural but refers to the genus and is applied even to a single woman in context. Imam Muhammad, on the other hand, argues that the plural must be given its minimal numerical significance of two, as in inheritance laws (الوصية أخت الميراث). Thus he divides the third into seven shares: three for the mothers, two for the poor, and two for the needy. This dispute extends to other examples: (1) bequeathing one-third to a specific person and half to the poor: the two again divide into shares giving half to the one person and half to the poor (interpreted as one recipient), while Muhammad divides the third into three parts: one for the person and two for the poor (since poor must be at least two). (2) Bequeathing specific amounts like 100 to Zaid and 100 to Amr, then including a third partner: Muhammad's principle leads to the partner getting one-third of each of Zaid's and Amr's shares in the first case, and half in the second case when the amounts differ. The passage concludes by noting that the understanding from the commentary and glosses is that the two's position (considering one individual from each group) is the relied-upon one.

Key Terms
الجمع المحلى باللام (al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam): A plural noun prefixed with the definite article 'al-', used to refer to a group or genus.
أخت الميراث (ukht al-mirath): The analogy that the rules of wills (وصية) are similar to inheritance (ميراث) in certain aspects, such as the interpretation of plural words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how many shares does the poor group receive when the testator bequeaths one-third to the mothers of his children (three) and to the poor and needy?
A) One share each.
B) Two shares each.
C) Three shares each.
D) The same as the two's opinion.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of the plural definite article in bequests is disputed within the Hanafi school; the relied-upon view is that it indicates the genus, so one from each group suffices.
